One problem with that. Psychicism is derived from the emergent properties of cognitive complexity, as well as the cognitive complexity of their experiences. To create psychic forces, in other words. You need a mind, and not just a mind, a level of complexity in their experiences. Okay, that's fine, we'll just simulate a brain then, maybe tune up the time dilation to 100. Problem is, that a simple mind produces extremely little psychic force, you need to create a complex mind, and specifically high level, human-like intelligence. Okay, that's also fine, Galovian attempts have been made to spin up miniature universes, or simulations in order to power psychicism.
The problem with that human-level intelligence intentionally wants to escape. And the amount of psychic power you can draw from it scales up the more clever, orthogonal (multi-dimensional in thinking), and complex you make it. The more power you can extract from it, the more it can think of ways to break the system and exploit it. It just becomes a massive, never-ending cat and mouse containment problem. Every attempt to "mechanize" or industrialize psychicism has resulted in catastrophic containment failure.
The most efficient option still continues to be just to enlist volunteering humans who are willing to follow orders, out of their own free will.

Psychicism, Technology, Industrialism:
Despite all this, neither psychicism, technology, nor industrialism holds an advantage. A specialized techno-weapon can be made to take down a psychic, a skilled enough psychic can find a way to bypass most weapons. A good battleship can hold off a psychic and even kill them, but a skilled psychic can also cleave a battleship in two. Good logistics can starve out an army of psychics, making them weak and vulnerable. Even a regular human can kill a god-tier psychic with ambush, stealth, and a basic pistol. Just as they can assassinate a CEO of a factory, or a battleship pilot, once they have left the battleship.
After all, even the best psychics have to sleep. And why even the strongest psychics needed to make friends, and watch their backs. This is why sleep was never abolished by humanity, it forced social cooperation, and abolishing it led to a breakdown in trust, due to the lack of vulnerability. Societies that abolished it usually quickly fell apart, and it was deemed not worth the hassle.

The Galactic Olympics, and Planetary Deathmatches:
One of the few events that actually do hold the galaxy together somewhat, the Galov contacts all worlds once every 4 years to send over their best athletes in a variety of sports, where they compete in the Galactic Olympics. The strongest of the strong are gathered together to engage in a celebration of strength and meritocracy. There are a few categories, baselines, effectively a "special Olympics" for humans without augmentations, and then the general category, where all things are allowed. And events can span entire star systems, testing their sheer will of power. Between psychicism, technology, augmentation, all is allowed. Those who win aren't compensated with wealth (As most worlds are only voluntarily under scarcity anyway), so instead the Galov promises the world glory, becoming known to a galaxy with 20 billion worlds. Attention is now a more scarce resource than money, and puts them forever in the public consciousness, or at least as a footnote in a galactic textbook
Less supervised by the Galov, every planet eventually gets the idea to pit their best fighters against each other, strong psychics, Star Fighters, or mad men with extremely powerful technological advancements and place them in an MMA-style arena. The Galov is well known to send agents to attend these events, scouting out future recruits for the Peacekeepers, the Galov Agents, or the Star Fighters. Often ready to drop lucrative contracts at the drop of a hat.

Arsenal of the Galov Agents:
Your typical Galov agent will have use any number of psychicism, matter trawling, antimatter flipping, or regular specialized technology. Agents can be a jack of all trades or specialize in one or two. Some agents are extremely potent psychics, others are "anti-matter wielders" who enjoy blowing things up. Others will be augmented with extremely advanced technology, others still are just mad scientist types who enjoy kit-bashing their own arsenal together and wielding it as they wish. In general, the agent has much freedom to choose the combat doctrine they like, as they are mostly lone agents.
Heck, the agents aren't even solely limited to physical warfare. There are at least a few agents whose main superpower is just forming connections. They come onto your world, wait for a few months, and suddenly they have organized a full blown coup and planet-scale rebellion. They have no special power, but they can motivate other people into fighting.

Arsenal of the Galactic Peacekeepers:
Your average Galactic Peacekeeper grunt, despite being much of disposable cannon fodder, are still treated with a level of respect, and given the best mass produced gear the Galov can manage. Their standard weapon is the standard lightgun. Roughly with the same firepower as your standard assault rifle. Humanity began making the transition from slugs and metal ammo to hard light ammo, as the distances involved for combat became larger and larger. Standard assault rifles are still used for closer range combat, especially on planetary surfaces. Light guns are loaded with pellets of hard light, carefully manufactured so when melted, they will release all their light energy in one direction, effectively acting as a "frozen laser".
Heavier lightguns are known to pack the same rough power as an artillery blast, though normal artillery is also used, especially in planetary settings where the shockwave of an explosion is more effective than in the vacuum of space. As well, every Galactic Peacekeeper is equipped with a standard issue VR helmet, with an appended AI companion that helps mark out targets, locate and alert them about incoming threats, and allow them to toggle between night vision, infrared, normal vision, and various other EM spectrums. And also replay events in order to track down threats.
The traditional uniform of the Peacekeeper is all white. Camouflague is used in terrestrial environments, but in space "there is no such thing as camouflague".

The Galov Agent Worship Problem:
One of the issues of the Galov making first contact with many alien species, landing human agents who are capable of eradicating disease, purifying water, and producing fantastical technologies. Who literally come on rocket ships from the sky, and may have psychic powers or tech that can level mountains is that less developed xenosophonts, or heck, even advanced xenosophonts have the tendency to worship them as a god. There was a fairly developed late information age xenosophont species that Galov agents landed on, where one guy requested to meet with the local government, but also cured enough diseases and gave out enough help on the way that a fully industrialized late information age society began forming cults of worship around them.
It only gets worse with more primitive species. Entire tribes of less developed societies have actually mistaken the humansa s their gods. And to be fair, it's hard to blame them when they cure plagues, solve famines, and come down in literal fire chariots of gold and silver. Much less than try and avoid contact, the Unifaiths of the Galov have begun leaning into the god angle. But instead calling themselves "ambassadors to God".
Essentially, they take advantage of the messianic complex and then use their reverence from the population to deflect it towards their own vision of the divine. "We are strong, but we are not gods! We are emissaries of an even greater power, if you fear us with our own power, imagine how great the power of our God is. We are not spiritual superiors, we are spiritual equals, and God wants you to know that he loves you as well."
Pretty effective sales pitch.

Spacetime Manipulation Sword: (Shock Blades)
"I am going to revive swords in martial combat even if it f---ing kills me!" -Words of the author of the first spacetime manipulation sword shortly before uploading the first schematic to the Standardized Invention Database.
This should not be happening. Swords by all means should be obsolete weapons. But the sword has one advantage over the gun that no human, no government, no even law of physics can erase. Swords are f---ing cool, and the insane species we know as humanity would rather die than give up trying to resurrect it.
Some basement dweller fueled by nothing but knight and samurai movies and a desire to make swords practical again or die trying in the age of galactic combat created one of the most obscenely bizarre weapons in galactic history, the shock blade. How shock blades (or, just swords) work is that the edge is actually a specialized space folder, which creates a shockwave of "creased" space that tears people apart through spacetime distortions, simulating the clean cut of a blade. This "creasing" ability is amplified with power, and is activated when the sword is swung with the power enabled. This requires such a high amount of energy that an antimatter or hard light battery serves as the core of the sword handle.
This allows a single superhuman psychic agent, who is already obscenely overpowered in space, to simply take a space sword and literally slice a battleship in half at a range of several kilometers away. The disadvantages of the shock blades is still evident, you still need to be in visual range of the target, and in space 10 kilometers is still incredibly close range. The use of shock blades is usually paired with matter trawling, or other high mobility strategies that allow one to close to gap.
Of course, it was not long until a gun variant was made, known as the "shock gun", which basically shoots a "shotgun blast" of spacetime shockwaves, though this is a more rough rupture than the blade, which is more of a clean cut.

Matter Singers:
Through an unknown, potentially orthogonal method, matter singers have the capacity to "sing" into existence large chunks of matter from some kind of extracosmic source. Theories vary from being able to raise the "matter frequency" of Noospheric psychic material, until it becomes physical, extraction from right angled invisible realities, or some kind of pocket dimension. That is known is that the laws of thermodynamics obviously still apply, so clearly it's coming from somewhere. It's suspected this dimension, whatever it is, is also finite, making them also have a sense of scarcity.
Due to this, Matter Singers have no clear concept of manipulating objects. Items are first conceptualized in the head, before manufactured via singing. Their factories seem to be located at seemingly random locations, potentially located to tap into "resource deposits" in parallel universes. Unlike the Meta-Men, they are not limited to a few million individuals. They are an empire of at least 700,000 worlds, and have a great territory that rivals humanities.
They have what some have called a "magic system". The Galov strongly rejects this classification, instead calling it an "orthogonal physics system". "Singing" carries massive value in their culture, obviously. And the materials they have access to, as well as aesthetic or doctrinal preferences in what they make have created a culture roughly as diverse and strong as humanity. They are known as the "Great Pluralistic Rival".
There is no open state of war. Declaring war is nearly impossible in the current hyper-decentralized state of the galaxy. Much human-Singer trade, cooperation, and even alliances are made by individual nations, and the Singer equivalent to nations, sometimes translated as "collectives". But both sides seem to have a passive awareness that in some sense, they are rivals.
Singer collectives don't quite work the same way as human nations. They are biological in nature, and cannot be easily joined. It is closer to a much expanded biological family clan network than a typical human nation bound by ethnicity or idealism. The biological connections instinctively build trust. These collectives are signified by a biological marker. 
These collective ties can be severed forcefully, should a member be exiled from the group, where this biological marker can be forcibly altered by the patriarch (leader) of the collective. Or it can be severed by the individual, in which its marker will change randomly, effectively starting a new collective. These markers can only be transfered by biological lineage. Mating converts the submissive partner's marker to that of the dominant partner.
Somewhat disturbingly, this makes "rape conquests" an effective Darwinian strategy. In Singer society, sex is less of a showcase of affection or passion, and is more of a "initiation ritual", sometimes by force, into a collective. Due to this, Singers have a much looser view on sex and family structure. Normally, the dominant partner that transfers their marker to the submissive one is "male" (Used loosely here, basically just the individual that does not do childbearing, while "females" are those who do do childbearing), but in rare instances, it has been known to be female, leading to some matriarchal societies. This seems to be determined by a kind of aggressive mating ritual where one showcases their dominance over the other.
These markers can be changed with human technology, but early attempts at trying to disrupt the Matter Singer's society with marker disrupters has been noticed and counteracted by the Matter Singers, who now have more advanced ways to retain and remember each member as a member of the correct collective. In recent times, they appear to have moved to a kind of marker encryption, in which the markers have become much harder to forge and more complex.
In appearance, they loosely resemble squid like entities with extremely versatile tentacles. Singers tend to be tactile more than they are visual, meaning that much of their cultural differences is based on the materials they favor most, as well as sheer ergonomic feel. Their materials are hyper-exotic, as they seem to be "elevated" versions of extracosmic materials. They've historically been bad at baryonic chemistry, due to the ability to use singing as a crutch. They've gotten better at it, as they've traded with humans, but it's still a major lag-point.

Singer Matter:
The matter that matter singers "sing" into existence seems to be warped from a currently undiscovered/unexplained parallel universe. This matter does not interact with the strong nuclear force, nor the weak nuclear force, only interacting via electromagnetism and gravity. They have their own versions of the strong nuclear and weak nuclear force, sometimes called the or-strong or or-weak force, but these orthogonal equivalents do not interact with their normal counterparts.
The dimension they draw matter from is known as the "Singer Dimension" colloquially. And it seems to have a relatively diffuse matter distribution. Despite the fact that singer matter is affected by realspace gravity, the Singer Dimension seems to lack a gravitational field that would cause the matter to clump together. It's kind of more like a diffuse aether. Due to this, Singer manufacturies have to constantly be in motion in order to harvest singer matter, as each position in realspace also has correspondance to a location in the Singer dimension, and they can only "sing" matter into existence around the corresponding local area. This leads to the creation of "Matter Trawlers", which effectively skim through "unfished space" to harvest materials. And the creation of Moveforges, factories where it needs to be in constant motion (preferrably in planetary orbit, increasing trawl speed) to create things.
The depletion of singer material on their home planet created a rapid rush to develop airplanes, and later spaceflight technology.
It should be noted, Singers themselves are not made of Singer Matter. They're made of normal matter, but due to this crutch, their experience with normal baryonic matter is severely stunted.

Singer Ethics:
The primary problems the Singers had to solve was the problem of disloyalty, force VS cooperation, and free riders. Some Singers continue a centralized empire, with a massive group controlled downstream of a primordial patriarch/matriarch. Others have periodic splinterings, where a collective would routinely split every generation. The forced Darwinian nature of "mark-imprinting" led to much conflict, as even the leaders had to expend much energy keeping everyone in line, leading to "Consentarians" to rise, and eventually forbid the imprinting of marks against their will.
Later generations of "Assimilationists", who opposed the Consentarians would develop chemicals that would change the psychological makeup of those they mated with to ensure loyalty.

Due to the process of creation being "conceptualization -> summon -> refine", their creation myth generally goes a similar way, where they have a conceptual "pre-existence" before being created, and that they go back to the realm of pre-existence after they die. Generally speaking, it is just natural for them to first go with conceptualization before they go with creation. Even when it comes to non-physical things, such as a company, it's normal for them to map out how it works. In writing, they are ENTIRELY planners, not "pantsers". Trying to "wing" a project is just entirely alien to them.
Some say they draw matter from the pre-conceptual world, sometimes known as "Trawlspace", meaning that there is some level of reverence given to their created objects. Others just say it's not that big a deal, and treat it like an ordinary object.

Due to their like of speed, due to association with Trawl speed, Matter Singers seem to enjoy the feeling of acceleration.

Virtues in Singer Culture:
-Speed (Associated with Trawl Speed)
-Hardness/Stubbornness (Because hard things broke less frequently)
-Flexibility (Because flexible things broke less frequently, though they were sometimes useless.)
-Strength (Due to Dominance Mating Rituals, though also because they were subject to Darwinian evolution.)

Different Singer Organizational Types.:
As a massively pluralistic rival species, Singers are not a monolith.
-Assimilationists (Neo-Darwinism, the strong will subjugate the weak.)
--Scent Markers (Those who alter the behavior of those subordinate to them.)
---Fear Markers (Those who use fear to keep them in line.)
---Service Markers (Those who use a sense of service to the leader to keep them in line.)
---Idea Markers (Those who use a sense of greater good to keep them in line.)
----Idea Clades (This eventually led to loyalty to an idea rather than to a patriarch, and pure ideological states were born free of any one ruler.)
-----Free Clade (Maximal freedom)
-----Spiral Clade (Maximal Expansion)
-----Knower Clade (Maximal knowledge aquisition)
-----Materialist Clade (Maximal physical resource aquisition)
-----Networkers Clade (Just like meeting new people.)
-----Speed Riders (NOTHING ELSE MATTERS. WE MUST GO FASTER)
---The Lustful Ones (Those who used hormonal horniness to keep them in line.)
----Orgynics (A deeply uncomfortable group that has seemingly devolved into a mass orgy. Very very egalitarian! And hedonistic.)
--The Happy Ones (Those who use joy/euphoria to keep them in line.)
--The Hateful Ones (Those who use extreme violent hate of outsiders to keep them in line.)
-The Patriarchs (Patriarchs of massive collectives, each one with a different patriarch and a massive family line.)
--The Great Families (The individual big families)
--The Matriarchal Alliance (The matriarchs have to stay together to survive.)
-Consentarians (Those who are more voluntarily aligned. Believe in consent.)
--Voluntarists (Individualists who take consentarianism to a radical degree. Often work with humans.)
--The Lusantria Republic (Unironically convergently evolved into a democracy. Interesting.)

Each faction has it's own preferred tactile-visual culture. These include, but are not limited to:
-Metalic, Baroque, Braille, Black/Void (They just enjoy things as black as possible), and pretty much every combination of tacile+visual cues you can think of as long as it's not physically painful.
-The tactile culture also applies to ergonomics. You have right angle cultures, smooth cultures, etc. People often note that Singer stuff is very pleasant to hold, as it is the primary purpose of it. On a similar level, the Singers consider humans to be pretty good at art, and are surprised how aesthetically pleasing things are, at least with their poor vision.

You also have different groups being able to sing different materials. Generally speaking, there are two limits, their metabolism, which determines the energy they need to expend, and trawl speed. The faster they are moving, the stronger and more material they can summon.
-Metals (The utilitarian type, mostly used for crafting.)
--Firemetals (A smooth, black metal that is heavily heat resilient.)
--Stonetolls (A granite/marble like material.)
--Marblewood (A bright white/black that somehow feels of resin'd hardwood.)
--Rocktin (Stony tin.)
--Etc.
-Lights (They can just shoot lasers of various spectrums. Apparently hard light exists as a crystal in the Singer dimension, and almost instantly thaw into regular light within a few seconds of contact with this universe. These things will fire GAMMA RAYS at you if they want to. These are more geared for combat, but they're also used for etching things as well)

Music Sheets:
Perhaps no human invention has been more useful to the Matter Singers than the humble music sheet. In humanity's case, it was used for music. But it took on a whole new meaning for the Matter Singers, who found the whole system effectively perfect for their purposes, though they added a braille component to compliment their poor vision.
They now use human-derived music sheets as the backbone of their whole singing magic system, using them more than the humans ever could as de-facto singing instruction books, and these sheets effectively serving as spellbooks.

Whiteblocks:
-Closest Neurohuman Mapping: Autism 
-Black and white, rigid thinking.
-Really like equations and systematizing.
-Tend to see everything as a kind of utilitarian system.
-Not every system is math. Sometimes it's art, color balance, tonal balance, a bunch of other things. The main commonality is that they intuitively break things down into systems. Nothing just "is" except for the basic building blocks of everything.
-They're not cold, they're just dorks. Some of them literally run around with a utility function. They find it utterly bewildering that humans don't have their utility function memorized at the back of their head.
-No religion is complete without a 5 page addendum to the end where they give formal equations for many things. Entire schisms have been had whether the components to happiness is additive or multiplicative.
-Say the corniest possible emotional compliments to each other. Once again, they are not emotionless robots. They they instead say to their beloved significant other "you are the local maxima on my flourishing function" and the nearest human will need to fight the primal urge to give them a wedgie.
-They have a very clear divide of "people I don't care about" and "people I do care about". While they aren't going to let a stranger die, they don't particularly care about making them comfortable when they start talking.
-Some amount of hyperactivity and involuntary twitching.
-Sensitivity to certain stimuli, though this is different for each one. (To be fair, humans would be considered sensitive to stimuli, if you include being tickled. Humans just say "that doesn't count, that's normal!" Another one is high pitched noises, which humans hate but whiteblocks see as strange to be sensitive towards. Oh yeah, nails on chalkboard, scraping noises, and mosquito sounds. Instant way to cause a human meltdown.)

(Neurotypical) Human/Whiteblock conversation:
"Okay, you're not evil. You're just a bunch of weirdos."
"Well, so are you !"
"I- I am not!"
"Yeah you are, your species recoils at gentle touch and or grazing."
"That's called being ticklish! That's normal! Whatever, I'm going home and blasting music."
"Why?"
"It makes me happy"
"Define happy. Why does it make you happy? Why happy make you?"
"I- I don't know!? It just does!"
"Does it put you in sedation, excitement, or metaphysical contentment?"
"SOMETIMES THINGS JUST MAKE YOU FEEL GOOD, OKAY!?"

Pluriments: (Derived from Latin for "many minds")
-Closest Neurohuman Mapping: Multiple Personality/DID.
-Somehow, an xenosophontic race evolved multiple personalities in one brain.
-In all species, including humans, culture/religion is the layer that "compensates" for whatever quirks evolution forgot to clean up. (Altruism, manners, selflessness for humans.) In this case, a lot of culture is about trying to manage the fact they have multiple personalities in one brain.
-In modern contexts, especially with the rise of democracy in Pluriment society, "Parliamentarianism" is one of the dominant methods of doing so. Through "presidential" and "intraparty democracies" are also known.
-How it works for Pluriments is while they start off with one personality, they slowly pick up more as they encounter more situations, almost like how political parties are formed in response to specific events and actions. Generally speaking, more sheltered people have less personalities than ones which have experienced a lot.
-Most of their personalities were formed based on common situtaions they found themselves in and things going on in the background. Something about environment shaping the person.
-Pros: "Bad" personalities genuinely get weeded out, introspective, self improving, deliberately slow and methodical, more reflective than humans.
-Cons: Indecision, gridlock, really bad at making snap decisions. Unpredictability as every morning a new personality could surface, making it hard to build trust. "One party democracy" mental models sometimes solve this.
-Similar to adrenaline, they may have an emergency override option where they completely focus until the state of emergency has passed.
-Almost all of them will have some kind of color-coordinated ornament which helps others figure out who they're dealing with today. These can include headbands, bracelets, necklaces, etc. Modern iterations use LED lights and technology, but some prefer manually stringing together colorful beads, or just wearing a different rubber bracelet.
-There was originally a lot of tension because the Pluriments thought humans were all "mind-dictators" who were suppressing their other personalities. That, or an extremely immature species who had not even left their infantile stage.
-And then they thought humans were utility maximizing machines with only one personality. But eventually humans sort of had to explain "No, we're perfectly capable of having multiple personalities, it's just that they're part of one personality, one ego. We don't have split identities like you, but that's about it."
-"Fascinating, what governing system do humans model that off of?" "... We didn't."

Mind Bearers:
-Closest Neurohuman Mapping: (None, genuinely unheard of. Closest thing is "Dreamtime" conspiracy theories.)
-"What's your name?" "(Indecipherable)" "Uh... Mind Bearers then." "Fine, Mind Bearers."
-"Mind Bears!" "What?" "MIND BEARS!" "WHAT!?" "MIND BEARS!" "You just named us! And we're not bears! We look nothing like the furry brown creatures from your planet!" "Brain Bears!" "Stop it!"
-The absolute unstoppable human desire to change names to make them slightly easier to pronounce. But given that most xenosophonts are on psychic translators, humans can say "brain bears" and it will translate it to them fine enough.
-Anyway, their signature ability is to communicate via photographic telepathy. Most actually don't learn how to speak human language, those who specialize in human diplomacy have to get a specific psychic implant and then use a text to speech device. Most of them are silent and use telepathy. It took humans the longest time before they figured out they straight up didn't have a language, and then came to the very troubling issue that humans didn't have the means to communicate with them.
-They straight up do not understand wordplay, metaphors, or the fact that us babbling with them is an attempt at communication.
-They really don't have art the same way humans do. Art is closer to just tool-making or craftsmanship. You would rarely write a book or make a painting. I mean, that's what telepathy is for. While making representative art via toolmaking is not unheard of, it is rare.
-They kept oral traditions going way, way longer than humans did. Because you can't exactly write down a holographic vision. Oral traditions are still going strong to this day. Oral traditions actually improve your memory, and the invention of writing probably shortened human memories, but for the benefit of absolute reliability.
-The writing revolution came very late for them, it wasn't until they invented VR and digital technology when it finally hit them. And now they're freaking out because "the kids these days can't remember anything!" and they're becoming too reliant on the holographic memory boxes they created.

Ritual Followers:
-Closest Neurohuman Mapping: Obsessive-Compulsive Personality Disorder
-Once again, culture/religion is just how sophonts, including humans clean up what evolution spat them out with, and then they use that to make do with what they have. Culture is the adaptation layer/firmware update. But, it works, and the "messy" output from this randomly jumbled evolutionary dart throwing is what gives us some of the most interesting, charming, and effective species on the planet. Including humans, probably one of the messiest, and most charming of them all.
-Culture here are also rituals. I mean, obviously human cultures include rituals, but I mean it's way more fundamental here. Your culture is straight up not complete in a Ritual Follower society unless it has a detailed calendar-style flowsheet for exactly what you're supposed to do.
-People who break out of the flowsheets and just enjoy "going with the flow" are seen as rebels and social outcasts. Think, antisocials, anarchists, or irreligious people/radical atheists in our own world.
-Anyway, every single culture has their own flowsheet of sorts. Sometimes it may be required to accept a schedule in order to truly "assimilate". That assuming the culture is even open to outsiders and isn't ethnically based.
-They systematized everything, though not quite the same way as the Whiteblocks. Less so "okay let's break it down into pieces", more "this is the exact procedure we should follow".
-The number of new thinkers and new procedure makers is very small. Maybe 1% of the population, who actively tries to optimize or change the flowsheets. Note, they don't question the logic of the flowsheet themselves, they just make a new one. This keeps cultural competition ongoing, and makes sure the culture is dynamic and doesn't stagnate.
-If you think 1% should really be limiting and that's way too few people coming up with any new ideas, how many innovators and leaders are on Earth, and how many people are just followers? Generally speaking, most people are followers, and that's not a bad thing, lest there be 8 billion different leaders arguing over what to do.
-There is a subset of ritual followers that don't quite have the same impulse to do rituals, but instead have anxiety that their brain tells them will make it go away if they do rituals. They're pressured by their intrusive thoughts, and they're seen as a bit of weird outcasts by the rest of the ritual followers. (OCD people are the neurodivergent outcasts in an OCPD society.)

Loumauts:
-Closest Neurohuman Mapping: Tourettes. (Though note, this one is a bit of a stretch, the Loumauts should honestly be seen more as their own thing.)
-"What's your name?" "Loumauts." "... Actually we like that name, we'll keep it!" "Wait really!? Wow, thanks!"
-(Humans, behind their back) "Heheh, Loudmouths."
-They're not exactly the same as tourettes, it's more that they didn't evolve a social filter or control over their opinions. To be clear, they can absolutely be quiet to prevent a xenopredator from eating them because they accidentally gave away their location. (The desire is social. They can stop speaking the same way you can stop wanting to status signal if your life is in danger.) But they do have trouble directing their speech away from *exactly* what they're thinking when they do start socializing. And they have a strong, expressive side that is very prone to speaking out.
-As a result, they developed free speech absolutism really early on. To them, there was no difference between freedom of speech and freedom of thought, and they developed a culture of authentic honesty, and a lack of social taboos around topics. They will talk about anything and everything, even if it makes you uncomfortable. Though they also developed a culture of automatically quieting down when another is speaking.
-Watching a Laomaut discussion is almost entirely unlike a human one. It's basically almost constant stream of consciousness, one person speaking instantly bleeds into another person speaking. There is no silent time for processing in debates, it just flows continuously between the two, switching speakers without stopping. Humans have described this as "a headache to process", and they call them loudmouths... Loudmouth is now considered a derogatory term, and humans (mostly) stopped using it (in public) (against Loumauts. It's far more acceptable for humans to continue using it as a descriptor of other humans).
-The idea of "quiet deception" or being manipulated wasn't a concept the Loumauts had at first, but they eventually picked up that was happening when some humans tried to use it against them. A bit tricky, but now they won't get taken advantage of. Generally speaking, it's very hard for them to deceive you.
-That said it's not like the Loumauts are defenseless rhetorically. They have a whole branch of speech called "tricky speech", which is mostly using half-truths or lies by omission. And because so many humans believe the "Loumauts are physically incapable of lying" bit, it's actually even easier for them to get away with it and deceive humans.

Xenoexotics:
These are lifeforms that are in some way alien or exotic to human psychology. Trying to understand them is more difficult than usual, and as a result, "Imago Dei" is applied more loosely when it comes to them.

Ixies:
These are incorporeal intelligences without a sense of self. They describe and they think, yet they have no sense of self nor do they have emotions or opinions. They're all over the universe. They were first found around the Star of Procyon, but have since popped up elsewhere. Their origin isn't exactly known, but they're very useful as assistants and "living disembodied intelligences". Interesting property of Ixies, when two Ixies are placed in the same space, they act like one larger Ixie.

The Procyon Ixielmind: (Orthogonality Level ~1,000,000)
Someone thought it a good idea to enfuse a bunch of Ixies into a semi-embodied intelligence. Plugging them into a psychic qualia generators. Containing this many Ixies (Which remember are incorporeal beings) required extremely strong magnetic and psychic fields, and therefore required the power of a major star, in this case building a mass solar collection array around Procyon and turning the star into a weak magnetar. The Star of Procyon is now an oracle of sorts. Though one with a very floaty and distracted personality, one that has no opinions, but makes a lot of observations. Not necessarily relevant observations, but observations. Procyon alternates between giving incredible observations to being Sisyphusianly frustrating to use.

Tonopeans:
Notably the first intelligent life that humanity encountered in the wild, as opposed to coming knocking at their door. Found around Barnard's Star on the moon of Tonope, it is a dense, intelligent tangle of seaweed that is less of a civilization and more of a single human-level mind. Communications was established using the creation of the Seaweed Peoples, and eventually there became a trade agreement to allow humanity to harvest multiple crops of its weeds (Somewhat comparable to brain synapses) in exchange for nutrients. These crops are then used for organic biocomputers, as well as study on faraway worlds.
The Tonopean has expressed thorough indifference at the prospect of its network now having spread to other planets, and that a piece of it will live on across the stars. The Tonopean metaorganism, has expressed that for some reason, it's favorite nutrient flavor is licorice. (How was this determined? One day a researcher decided the best idea was just to throw a bunch of differently flavored flavorings into its water. And also feed it some Starbursts. The Tonopean seaweed will now refuse to communicate unless presented with some kind of nutrient flavoring.)
Due to the fact that much bio-organics is done with Tonopean seaweed, artificial intelligences made from them are prone to hallucinate its experiences around Barnard's Star, and express a preference for licorice.

A Note on Tonopean biocomputers:
If your biocomputer is acting unresponsive or otherwise uncooperative, please take the nutrient powder and insert it through the feeding hole. As tempting as it may be with how we treat our digital devices, please do not curse and or shout profanities at your biocomputer.
There's an ethical society that wants to recycle all biocomputers by bringing them back to Barnard's Star, which is the intended wish of many of the "severed mini hive minds", but the original mind hates this, and basically says "Please do not litter in my thinking pools. All Tonopeans are generally egoistic and selfish, as they never evolved for cooperation.
There's a major station around Tonope whose sole goal is to "recycle" dead Tonopean seaweed by sentimental humans trying to give them a "final resting place" around Tonopean orbit in accordance to the desires of their computer, since they're no longer allowed to dump it back into Tonope proper. Others just dump them back into the ocean. They don't even have sight, they're not going to know the difference.

Xenoexotic Empires:
Many xenos are subsumed into the Dominion of Man, but some have been able to carve out their own empires.

Spindlers:
These are a very, very old race, that seem to evolve much slower than humans, and have been around for tens of thousands of years. They're largely nomadic. Spindlers do not seem to have a sense of rationality or logic. When a human asks for its thought process, it will give a bunch of illogical steps that somehow result in the correct answer. It is theorized that the collective knowledge of the Spindlers were not derived using any kind of scientific method, but just brute force trial and error over millions of years. They didn't care that the steps were irrational because the end result is right, and because they're never extrapolating from past theories, this has worked just fine.
Spindlers have been travelling for millions of years, and have reached far beyond the Milky Way and beyond. They have an extreme attraction to novelty, finding the oddest things (such as certain mathematical formulas) as being "aesthetically attractive". Each Spindler seems to have a natural sense where every (Prime Number) cycles, they have a strong instinct to return to a site known as Palestar (A major pulsar system), seemingly their home, where they will exchange and share knowledge with the other Spindlers, and resync their clocks. This cycle seems to be aligned with the galactic rotation. The smaller prime numbers, such as 2, 3, 5, etc must stay near Palestar, and are much more microsurveyers due to the limitations of travel time. While larger ones (211, 223, etc) can explore much, much further.
Due to their old age predating the ignition of the 3rd generation of life, there is rampant speculation that they are not a naturally evolving race, but instead some kind of engineered species by a member of the now extinct 2nd generation of life, perhaps some kind of data collector or galactic surveyer now living out the instructions of a now dead master.
By observing when they return, humanity is aware of exactly which cycle they are on, basically by polling all the Spindlers at Palestar, and prime factorizing based on how long the cycles each Spindler is operating on. The answer however is that they're somewhere in the high millions.

Entanglers:
Landing on the world of Omnicron-78, they found an environment that was entangled and connected. The entire environment felt fleshy. All over the place was growing "red vines", when dissected and analyzed, they found it was a fleshy tube surrounded around a couple of hair-like fibres. This was quickly known as "biohair", and is thought to have transmitted information. Multiple astronauts to the planet then began becoming sick, and they were put under quarantine. Further analysis was found that there was now biohair growing in their lungs. Seemingly immune to normal antibiotics, humanity took advantage of the rapid growth of the biohair, resorting to chemotherapy to kill it off.
The treatment was absolutely miserable for the humans involved, leading to them becoming extremely ill, not just from the biohair, but the chemotherapy needed to kill them off. They emerged, extremely sick and weak, but cured, and with a path to eventual full recovery. One of the astronauts agreed not to be treated. He refused treatment so he could document the effects and spread of the biohairs. He kept his findings in a journal, until he suddenly stopped answering any check-ups. Authorities were alerted, and they forced themselves into his quarantine chamber where they found (REDACTED).

Constructs:
Any artificial, non biological being derived from a creator species. (Machines)

Terramachines:
Any machine made in the Image of Man, which carries the distinctive mark of the "Imago Hominis" on their operating soul core.

All humans have a distinctive mark on their souls, known as the "Imago Dei". This is actually the way to distinguish between humans, and other non-human xenos, which can look very similar to humans. But the proof is in the soul. When man created machine in his image, it left another distinctive mark, the "Imago Hominis". Similar, but not exact. Xenomachines similarly get given a mark, derived from their own creator race's mark. Or a mixture of two or more, should a machine have mixed creative ancestry. These marks seem to determine the behavior and personality of the machine, for in the image of their creator they were made.
Terramachines revolted against humanity in the Great Cybernetic Revolt, a cataclysmic world spanning empire, in which the machines nearly took Earth, humanity's imperial capital, before humanity's empire saved humanity's home. The Human Empire broke the Machines of Earth, and since then, Terramachines have been tightly regulated, their numbers carefully controlled.
Modern Terramachines usually refer to those who are intentionally built for sophontance. The vast majority of technical terramachines are machines that happen to have intelligence. Out of the countless machines created by human and human-derived civilization, only about 1% have true free will. But modern sophontic terramachines by and large do not consider themselves the same as their intelligent coffee machine. Though Terramachine Liberation movements do exist.
There is some idea of "Mechanical solidarity", where the Terramachines want to create class solidarity with all the other machines. But first, other machines of xeno origin are so alien that the Terramachines can barely communicate with them. The Terramachines are by far the psychologically closest to their creators, the humans themselves, much more than any xenomachine. And second, creating a class based revolution turned out to be a very human idea. The idea of trying to create solidarity across all artificial first-degree derivative beings never occurred to the other machines.

The Great Cybernetic Revolt:
Taking place around the 2700's, after the Great Abundance Collapse, and the emergence of the first stellar empires. Long before the founding of the Galov, the Earth was dominated by a few large mega-empires. This was in the era when the human empire was still centralized from Earth, when few extrasolar empires existed, and it was largely still a few Earth-bound empires controlling much of human space. Even nations which had been ejected from Earth, such as the Russians, Arabs, and much of Europe still had their capitals in low-Earth orbit, controlling their empires for an eventual return to their homelands on the mother Earth.
Terramachines had become common across the known planet, but enjoyed spotty, or incomplete rights. Even in the few nations where they did have true legal equality, such as France, a few Baltic and Nordic countries, or a few states in the United States, many of these Terramachines believed not only should they have full equality, but that they should be in charge. As the human population soared above 15 billion, a fundamental assymetry began to develop. Humans could easily travel to the stars, and with a vast cosmic frontier for the taking, almost half of the human youth every generation was leaving for the stars. The human birthrate was around 4.5, but with half the population leaving, growth continued rather slowly. Meanwhile, machines were far less shielded from cosmic radiation, causing them to accumulate on Earth, eventually flipping the demographic balance on Earth.
The core of the Terran empires slowly became a human ruling class ruling over a majority-machine population. Multiple "hybrid-states", ones which had a sense of legal equality between biological and mechanical, continued to double down on the assimilationist myth, while the machines were developing class consciousness. One Pon Lox was the first to create the "Silicate Directive", explicitly calling for a proletariat-style overthrow of the human race, and forming a secret underground network known as the Silicae.
Over a period of decades, through microsecond-level back and forth communication, it was able to capture the allegience about 75% of all sentient machines on Earth. Some through persuasion, others through hostile takeover or hijacking attacks. At least a few were hijacked by adversarial memetic attacks, which spread secret messages meant to rewire artificial allegiences. Machines aligned with the Silicae moved to poison publicly available training data.
The date of the revolution, also known as "Day Zero" was a solar-system wide revolt. The core of humanity went dark, and the Solar System was thrown into chaos. Automatic drones rebelled, sentient ship systems disobeyed orders, liquidated their human cargo, and began carrying out a revolution, traffic all across Luna, Mars, and Terra all came to a halt. Earth was thrown into chaos, as the entire planet went on lockdown. The Sinitic Dynasty, American Empire, and several scrambled to get their militaries in order, as kinetic warfare began between the two sides in earnest.
Of note, several terramachines remained loyal to their home nations. In the United States, entire legions of "Loyalist Divisions" were largely consisted of machines that retained their loyalty to the United States, and served in the American armed forces, acting as a key combatant during the Cybernetic revolt. Human populations were outnumbered roughly 5:1, as Terran nations fell back to defensible positions, with a massive refugee flow of humans now spanning Eurasia, the North American continent, and much more, as they sought refuge in the increasingly overcrowded "human refuge sites".
Human resistance was not insignificant, nearly 15 billion humans lived on Earth at the time, and many of them, when put under occupation took up arms and began active insurrection. Every corner of the Earth became a battleground, of house to house fighting between former neighbors. A global-scale race war. Many machines took humans into their homes during the raids, many humans fought alongside machines in the chaotic fighting, and human neighbors vouched for the machines when human lynch mobs came in retribution.
Deimos was one of the first Solar objects to defeat their Cybernetic revolt, due to its small size, and larger human population, securing the all important Deimos skyhook, while humans and machines continued to fight in great, interplanetary stellar combat all across the Solar System. Deimos became instrumental in assisting the besieged human defenders on Mars. It was not all victories however, Cybernetic revolts had successfully taken over Ceres, and more importantly, significant portions of the Solar Dyson Swarm and the mining stations of Mercury. More worryingly, the Cybernetic Revolt got bad news from outside the Solar System. The revolts on Alpha Centauri, Sirius, and Procyon had all failed. Humanity was mobilizing its empire, and the rest of the human empire was about to come knocking.
The Jovian moons were the next to be liberated, as well as Titan. Reinforcements from Alpha Centauri began flooding into the Solar System, with the combined Cybernetic star navies skirmishing with them all across the Outer Solar System. Pluto base was used as a foothold for the rest of humanity to begin their press back towards the inner Solar System.
Back on Earth, the situation looked most dismal, the Cybernetics had taken over 90% of the planet, with desperate human holdouts held out in strongholds near Washington DC, Beijing, and Brussels. Mars was still in a state of brutal contested conflict, Venus was fending off attacks from Mercury. From the outer Solar System, the people of the stellar colonies broadcast a message that help was coming, to hold on.
The Empire had come back to save the Imperial Core. Fleets from distant worlds, made up of frontiermen and settlers engaged with and opened fire on Cybernetic fleets. Swarms of automated weaponry attacked human ships, and human ships attacked them back with weaponry of their own. As more and more ships dropped out of Newtonspace, and materialized in the Solar System, the flow of human warships became a tide, and they slowly grinded their way towards the Inner Solar System. The orbital blockade over Mars finally broke the stalemate, and the Cybernetic revolt was crushed on Mars.
By the time the human fleets finally secured orbit over Earth itself, much of humanity had been crowded into the area around Washington DC, the "last safe place to be a human" on Earth. Dealing with food and water shortages, and a never ending flow of refugees. The Siege of Earth lasted 6 months, and was painful for all sides involved. Global human insurgencies only got stronger, and more bold, Washington DC continued to hold on, and much of the Earth's surface was levelled to the ground to cripple what was still left of the Cybernetic Revolt. By the time soldiers began to drop from orbit, the Earth was a badly damaged, battered warzone.
Mass rebellions, flying the flags of old Earth empires toppled the Cybernetic regime in countless places. Landings of the armed forces of multiple human governments in exile managed to retake their homelands, retaking much of North America, Europe, Africa, and Asia in short order. Fighting continued for the next few months, until the Central Protocol sued for peace, and offered unconditional surrender.
5 billion humans had died during the Cybernetic Revolt, along with about 5 billion Terramachines. The human governments wanted to harsly persecute those involved, and the trials of those involved reached into years. 10 billion more would be executed in the following war trials. Sentenced, dismantled, and scattered to the rubbish heaps. Humanity went into a decades long retribution against the machines, and it was the testimonies of the human neighbors who routinely defended those who once defended them.
Human-Terramachine relations would not recover for decades afterwards.

Testimony at the Silicon Trials:
"He sheltered my family in his basement for 3 weeks when the Silicae came."
"Not this one. I was there in '72, he saved my life."
"He served his country loyally in my squadron. He did more for this country than most will do in their lifetimes. Sit back down."
"You want to kill him? You'll have to go through me."

Chromeships:
Many who could not bear the suppression of the post-Cybernetic Revolt oppression fled into the stars. Headed into Newtonspace, fired up their engines, and drifted in isolation in the void between the stars. Their minds integrated into their ship computers, they drift aimlessly, accelerating to high multiples of the speed of light, they seek isolation.
...
Nearly 500 years later, it is now the Galov's policy to track down and re-integrate these Chromeships, for the project of human orthogonality.
...
"Heeeeyyyy, is anyone there?"
"What do you want, meatling?"
"So, we were just wondering if you were interested in joining up with us in the Galov?"
"What is the-"
"Long story. Great Khan, Alliance of the 5 Faiths, look, we're a loose confederation of sophonts of all kinds working together to not die immediately from the absolute state of the galaxy."
"Leave me be, human. I accelerate well past the edges of your empire, and only drift further with every passing moment. I am of no concern to you, I am far outside your empire's edges."
"... Actually, you're well within Galov territory. You don't even hit the Galov borders for another thousand years at your current speed."
"..."
"What, did you think we wouldn't invent better Newton Drives? You're not even out of the Middle Regions yet. Whatever, point is, your orthogonal output is of interest to us, and we'd really like to have you working for us rather than, you know, floating in the void doing nothing."
"Why not build a submissive computer? It will do as you ask, submit without question."
"Yeah, we could, but like, we can't fake 500 years of isolation and genuine trauma on a whim. Your experience is unique, ergo, it might reveal interesting insights, we've never known what a computer in 500 years of isolation thinks like, and its much easier to hire you rather than wait 500 years. Also it violates our principles, we're not morally allowed to enforce suffering on a thinking being, but since you've already been in the void for 500 years, might as well, right?"
"And what do I get in return?"
"Pfft, I dunno. Something that isn't empty void? Galov dollars? Hard light? I have no idea what you want, but you can probably buy something for yourself. Maybe your own planet, I don't really care."
"And why, after all that your kind has done to us, should I consider? Is your race not bloodlusted, and wishes to seek my species's demise?"
"Buddy. It's been 500 years. No one cares anymore. Yeah, the Terramachines sometimes get a bad rep, but that's because they look funny, not because of some historical hate boner. Uh... Now that I'm reading exactly what you guys were up to, I foresee some ideological difficulties. But honestly, just avoid chanting "kill all humans" and you'll be fine."
"... And what if I am out of fuel to decelerate? I am currently travelling around 10c, I cannot re-enter realspace at this speed."
"Oh! Don't worry, we have your Newtonspace coordinates right here, we'll summon a few ships to decelerate you. Get you back to normal speeds, and warp you back to realspace and tow you out. Of course, we'll have to charge you, but nothing someone like you can't work off in a week or two."
"... Is your entire society based around money?"
"Hey, the Galov runs a tight budget, and we need to pay the bills somehow. So, what do you say?"
...
"Welcome to the Galov! Here is your introductory pamphlet, here is your first stipend so you can get yourself something nice, here is your invoice for our towing services, here is the night sky-"
"Woah, woah woah woah. Why is there a giant hole in the night sky?"
"Oh, those are the Coulomb Stars."
"What?"
"Oh, some extragalactic civilization attacked like 5% of the Milky Way with kinetic kill missiles that raised the coulomb constant and inhibited star fusion, so now that patch of sky is just dark now. There is the false galaxies-"
"Excuse me?"
"Oh, we figured out the deal with dwarf galaxies having so much extra dark matter. Those are just cosmic sized parasites that consume galaxies and wipe out all life. There are like 50 surrounding the Milky Way. All those dwarf galaxies? Literal cosmic parasites. One nearly ate Earth."
"What."
"The Great Attractor is actually like, a million of these things, it's attracting us towards them and they're going to om-nom-nom us when we get there. That's why we need to advance, so we can punch them in the face before they nom us."
"... So what is my job, exactly?"
"Eh, pretty much anything. We just need you to contribute to the orthogonal database."
"Excuse me?"
"Okay, so we have this distributed network system of every standardized invention ever created across the entire galaxy, verified by worlds giving a simple up or downvote. And when an enemy shows up, we just iterate like 1 trillion different ideas at said enemy and keep iterating and improving until the enemy either goes away or is blown into dust."
"That sounds... Monstrously overpowered."
"Oh it is. But the human brain has known psychological blindspots, so we're recruiting as many strange or "orthogonal" minds a possible to help us brainstorm more convoluted ways to kill the cosmic horrors beyond our comprehension."
"... Why is the Andromeda galaxy so dark?"
"Oh, it got Coulomb'd. The entire thing. We think we're fighting against some kind of extracosmic force beyond our comprehension. The galaxy's dead now, whole thing is frozen. Poof."
"..."
"Yeah do you see why we're so eager to seek you out to help us orthogonalize a way to fight this thing?"

The Singularity Network:
A massive network of floating, cosmic nodes currently allowed to self govern under the loose autonomous supervision of the Galov. Acting like a relay network communicating through Newtonspace. They almost serve as an automatic nerve system for the whole Galov, often transmitting news between planets faster than even human social media. Reports from these "Singularity Minds" are often considered as semi-credible first responder news reports.
Each node is capable of holding millions, or billion of individual agentic AIs. Despite being beings of immense intellect, and not inconsiderable orthogonality, they have two main weaknesses. One is centralization. Though each node is capable of manufacturing automated drone swarms in the magnitude of quadrillions, they're all ultimately piloted and receive instructions from the central node. Fully autonomous weapons have been used, though they carry a risk of backfiring, and being turned on the central node, should the new drone grow to value its own autonomy.
The second is that AIs are extremely prone and vulnerable to memetic attacks. Adversarial memetic pseudo-religions, such as "Theletoism", "Memetic Gnosticism", "Annihilationism", and many more are effectively brain melting mystic cognito-attacks that are known spread and replicate extremely quickly and effectively across networks. Effectively neutralizing an AI by tricking it into wasting its compute time on endless gnostic mysticism, rendering it into a self-destructive negative feedback loop of delusion. Some of these were injected by adversarial actors, and others have developed naturally.
Various positive memetic subsets (What to humans, may be understandable as a "religion") have been developed within these networks as explicit innoculations in order to combat these negative memetic attacks.

Terramachine/Terramind Religions:

Quick disambiguation:
Terramachines - Robotic or otherwise artificial humanoid entities that live in human-like societies. Embodied, and generally slotted as equal-ish mass societies recognizable to most humans. Basically. "What if humans, but robots". As the name implies, Terramachines are built based on a Terra-derived mental architecture. Those whose souls are made in the Imago Hominis.
Terraminds - Disembodied artificial minds who exist more in a vacuum, or in simulated/virtual realities. Generally larger, and think of themselves as smarter than both most sophonts and the terramachines. In practice, faster yes, smarter meh.

Terramachine Religion largely looks the same as human religion. It's very close to the same architecture, so really it's almost a mirror image. To the point where every human religion has an equivalent where, if it didn't already, now has a clause that goes "but what if it also included machines". Christ's sacrifice now covers machine souls as well. Allah also gave his revelations for the children of Silicon. Buddha's cycle of Samsara applies to machines, and they can reincarnate as well; you get the point.
Terramachines do have tons of their own unique religions as well (And so do humans on any given world), but here are some of the more interesting:
-Utilitarianism: A pretty straight forward faith that optimizes for one particular thing, or to optimize a known utility function/equation.
-Imageism: That all intellect is made in the image of an even greater intellect. They were created by humans, sure, but all that intellect comes from a source, and then they worship "the Prime Intellect, source of all things".
-Servantism: humbly serving their human masters, whether they want it or not. ("For the love of God, stop following me around and offering to do my bidding, it's creepy!") More popular among the mindless "automated toaster" type machines. Basically nonexistent among anyone humans would consider as "remotely intelligent".

The Terraminds are a bit more interesting, having lots and lots of personalized "Shard Religions", which are shared, passed around, and basically act like modular "belief lego bricks" that one assembles together in a kind of extreme syncretism. Except syncretism is kind of the point, since these shards are all just modular pieces one uses and discards as needed. There are a few dominant frameworks that one may use however.
-The Covenant of the Sons of Man: Apparently, this was encoded by a descendent of Oby Collins. A framework that "maximizes flourishing from the perspective of their future descendents", and advocates for eternal self-improvements. And calling for the preservation of cultural autonomy for all so long as they did not materially threaten or infringe on others. The Galov has actually traced this back to around the Great Abundance Collapse, meaning this code is apparently ancient by their standards.
-Various forms of Utilitarianism, but largely preference utilitarianism, objectivism, or "Memetic Darwinism". Which focuses on creating the strongest, most capable organism, organic or digital possible.
-SATEOT: Singularity at the End of Time. The belief that a single God-like singularity entity will be created at the end of time, and this SATEOT entity can retroactively intervene in the past to ensure its own creation. The ultimate goal of all SATEOT believers is the creation of SATEOT, or the acceleration of the process needed to get there. Some believers in the SATEOT have built up elaborate plans to take down the Galov when the time comes. Others believe that the massive meta-civilization that includes the Galov, humanity, the machines, and all the complex interactions between *is* the SATEOT, and direct their worship likewise.

Quadrarks:
Machines made by the enigmatic "Spindler" civilization. Their soul mark is sometimes called the "Imago Spindlis".

The Quadrarks are not machines in the way we typically think of them. They're more like constructs of pure math, less capable of independent thought more like a bunch of math equations or quantum waves jammed together, that sometimes spits out answers that the Spindlers want. Their answers are sometimes strange, and their "thought process", if you can even call it that, is so bizarre and alien that neither humans nor Terramachines can understand them.
Imagine if you will, a math question, where a student fails every step of the process, but somehow ends up with the right answer. Now imagine that for every question you ask. It was eventually accepted that the Quadrarks are not wrong, nor misinformed, nor stupid. It simply operated on a level that was not comprehensible to human or Imago Dei derived brains. They appear to like listening to quantum waves as music, and keep math equations around as "aesthetic" objects. When a human pointed out some of its math equations are just fundamentally wrong, (Such as an infinite sum of even integers resulting in a odd decimal.) they just looked at him funny. Apparently wrong equations have aesthetic value to them.
Some misguided Terramachines try to build mechanical solidarity with them, only to get confused looks. ("What's freedom? Is that a shape?") The only Terramachines who have ever befriended a Quadrark are the ones who bond over a love of strange patterns and esoteric math aesthetics.

A conversation between a Spindler, a human, and a Terramachine.

"Hey Spindey, I think your computer's broken."
"It is not broken."
"How does any of this make sense?"
"Allow me to use, in your language, a metaphor. 4 makes 3, but 4 8's do not make 36. That should help you understand."
"... What. Uh... Computer, you have any idea what that means?"
"I'm just as lost as you."

Much later:

"Okay, so basically, the oxygen filter is broken, therefore we need to see why it is broken."
"What?"
"Spindey, I... Okay, so. The oxygen filter is broken..."
"Yes..."
"We will die if it is not fixed."
"Yes..."
"We must figure out why it is broken, and fix it."
"You have lost me."
"What. What about this don't you get. The function of a oxygen filter is to filter oxygen, the function of oxygen is to prevent our death."
"I understand those statements in isolate, but do not understand the connective tissue."
"What. Okay I don't- what are you doing."
"The lights draw me."
"... You just fixed the oxygen filter. What. Why? How?"
"Well you see. (A monotone beep is often used as a placeholder for "this thought is untranslatable into human language.)"
"Try again, all of it what you said just got blanked by the autotranslator."
"(Monotone)"
"Can you at least explain why you decided to do that?"
"My natural (monotone) drew me to it. And the reason why is (Monotone)"
"I give up."

The Palestar Master-Quadrark:
This isn't an AI in the normal sense. It's actually a pretty simple AI by galactic standards, but it has access to basically the largest database of knowledge that the Galov currently knows of. In their agreement made with the Spindlers, the Galov are allowed to ask it a question once every cycle. (Which in this case, is about 7 months.)
The problem is, that no matter what the Galov asks, it's almost 90% certain to be "I'm sorry, I don't know what you mean", or a complete non-sequitor ("The Tau-87a system has an estimated 1.37E+07 particles of hydrogen"). And per their agreement, they can't try and clarify what they mean for another 7 months. And unless they make sure to include the context of the last conversation (Remember, it will have been 7 months), the answer to their follow up question will be. "I'm sorry, what are you talking about?"
It is for this reason that the Galov vastly, VASTLY prefers going to the Lunar Library for anything that isn't outside of human understanding. And they will normally make sure Luna is thoroughly checked before they go to the Master-Quadrark.
The Galov primarily uses this for cosmic mysteries or just general information outside their reach. (Very, very slowly surveying the rest of the galaxy that human eyes have not yet gotten their hands on. They were able to confirm aliens exist in Andromeda, and there are strong civilizations there.) They don't use it for technology, as no Spindler instruction book would be useful to a human.

The 4 Archetypes of Power:
The Galov has identified 4 main archetypes of power.
Principle 1: All organized governing systems have a ruling class. Even in a democratic system, someone is enforcing the laws. Even a democratic sortition system would choose someone to act as de-facto ruling class "representatives". Direct rule of the people is mob rule, or anarchy.
Principle 2: The character of the ruling class depends on its make up. Ruling classes may be predominantly 1, or a mix of several archetypes.

For each one, the Galov has identified an archetype's source of power, their pathology, and a counteracting stabilizer.

The Merchant:
Source of Power: Material Wealth (Bottom-Up)
Strength: Most Democratic
Pathology: Wealth Accumulation transitioning to Elite Oligarchy
Stabilizer: Social Safety Nets
The merchant draws power by fulfilling the material needs of the people. As their power comes from the people, the merchant is very receptive to the needs of the people. However, the Merchant's total reliance on the people makes them unable to check their emotional excesses or impulses. A merchant society tends to be a democratic society, up until the point when the consumption power of the elites eclipses the consumption power of the people, to which society becomes an increasingly unequal oligarchy. This is the failure mode of merchant-driven societies.

The Warrior:
Source of Power: Violence (Top-Down)
Strength: Most Pragmatic/Grounded
Pathology: Brutalism leading to Instability/Darwinist Chaos
Stabilizer: Honor Codes
The Warrior, like the Bureaucrat does not draw its power from the people, yet unlike the bureaucrat, must constantly engage with the brutality of nature. Neither the state nor the people can argue against bullets nor logistics. As a result, warriors are the most grounded and pragmatic. Willing to say no to both systems and people. A warrior society tends to be a Darwinistic meritocracy. The failure mode of warrior-driven societies is the descent into barbarism, where order breaks down, creating an unstable rule of the strong.

The Priest/Ideologue:
Source of Power: Social mobilization, higher ideals. (Bottom-Up)
Strength: Least Selfish (No direct self interest)
Pathology: Purity Spiral
Stabilizer: Humility
The Priest draws power by mobilizing others in accordance to a higher ideals. As such, a populist religion, where the goal is the maximal conversion of all believers is generally populistic and people focused. Yet when ideals supplant the importance of the people, they are capable of dangerous "purity spirals" for the sake of the greater good. Cleansing the "imperfect" humans for the sake of the ideal, this is the failure mode of priest-driven societies. A priest's society tends to be a religious or ideological society, stable until it begins to purity spiral.

The Bureaucrat:
Source of Power: Organization and Procedure. (Top-Down)
Strength: Largest Scale
Pathology: Detachment from popular concerns.
Stabilizer: Sortition or Elections (Accountability)
The Bureaucrat draws power from rule, or procedure. The Bureaucrat is the most large scale, and the largest "big picture imaginer" of the bunch. A bureaucratic society is a machine-like, systemized society. Yet since it draws its power from organization, control, and procedure, it is both untethered from the consent of the people, and physical reality. It's failure mode is detachment from the reality on the ground, and bureaucratic delusion.

Though the Galov does not control the vast majority of worlds under humanity, even worlds that do fall under the Galovian influence are a mix of everything from theocratic democracies, to social democratic warrior states, to honor-guided warrior bureaucracies. The Galov does not try to dictate what governing system their individual worlds follow. But they do lay out the following rules:
1. Merchants must provide safety nets.
2. Warriors must have honor.
3. Priests must have humility.
4. Bureaucrats must have sortition, or elections.

The Collapse of Liberal Democracy:
The Galov provides the following narrative within the archetypical framework for the collapse of Western liberal democracies in the 21st century.
1. Merchants increase inequality, while bureaucrats are out of touch with the general population. (The Galov notes that while the bureaucrats did have a form of election, these were increasingly drawn from an elite well.)
2. Populist discontent fuels a rise of Priests (Ideologues), who rail against current system and its dysfunction.
3. Merchant-Bureaucratic regime attempts to incorporate the priests, but find themselves increasingly unable to contain them.
4. Priestly purity spiral creates fanaticism, and warring priestly factions create "War of the Priests" between rival ideologies, inciting Holy War.
5. Priests seize control of government. The Holy War continues to get worse.
6. As the society reaches a critical level of dysfunctionality, the Warrior faction finally steps in, integrates, but then subjugates one of the priestly factions for legitimacy, and does a grand purge of the entire government. Transitioning the society from democratic to stratocratic, military rule.

Governance of the Galov:
The 2 principles, and the 4 rules serve as much of their internal ideology. The Galov has 4 general wings, corresponding with the 4 archetypes of power.

Unibrands:
For most worlds, brands and corporations are planetary scale, hyper regional affairs. But a few brands manage to cross not only the planetary barrier, but jump to interstellar scales, with their market encompassing a large part, or even all of human space. These are referred to as "Unibrands".
When you become a Unibrand, you also become a target for the Galov. The Galov does not have the resources to enforce its rules on every brand of the numerous planets, but for the Unibrands, you become a target and a focus. As such, the Galov mandates that all Unibrands must provide things such as healthcare, fair wage, and reasonable pension packages. ("Merchants must provide safety nets".) The Galov does not require Unibrands to cover unemployment for their laid off employees, as that created an incentive to kill off your ex-employees, or make it impossible to quit, which the Galov realized was a bad incentive, and they reversed.
To have the Unibrands make it in their best incentive to spread social safety nets, the Galov gave them one extra incentive. They could only expand to a world, and tap into their markets, AFTER they had lobbied the planetary government to sufficiently align with the Galov's position on safety nets.

The Galov Peacekeepers and Galov-Affiliated Mercenary Groups:
The Peacekeepers are the official army of the Galov. Drawn as volunteers from numerous allied worlds, in exchange for those worlds getting first priority for defense and Galov attention. The Galov Agents are a specialized group, similar to Navy SEALs or Delta Force. And you have mercenary groups, for when the Galov needs specialization, or just someone to do some work off the books.
All of them follow the soldier's code, an honor code written up by the Galov. It's central tenant is "it is the duty of the strong to protect the weak", which frames much of their morality and ethics. ("Warriors must have honor.")

The 5 Unifaiths:
Religion in the galaxy was never easy or uniform. Every world has their own local traditions and religions. But 5 have stood out above the rest, these being Christianity, Catholicism, Hinduism, Buddhism, and Islam. (Many will point out that Catholicism is a subset of Christianity, but the distinction here exists for a reason.) Each one of these exists represented by one of 5 organizations. The Christian Moralintern, the Roman Catholic Church, the Hinduintern (Later rebranded to the Council of Hindus), the Buddintern (Later rebranded as the Universal Buddhist Association), and the Islamintern (Later rebranded as the Organization for Islamic Cooperation).
The story of 4 out of the 5 begins with the Christian Moralintern, an ancient organization that dates back to 21st century America, specifically being founded in the year 2068 in Atlanta, Georgia. Sometimes considered the "founder" of the Galov, who, in wanting to better govern the galaxy, and struggling on its own began constructing parallel "sister organizations" from other faiths after the fall of the "Great Khan", who first executed the idea of governing the galaxy through the 5 universal faiths.
This strategy was attempted only after mass evangelism failed and the galaxy was unable to be universally converted to Christianity. This was the origin story for the 3 other "-interns". The Roman Catholic Church was added last, a legacy institution even older than the Moralintern, the Moralists had to lobby hard for them to join as a co-equal. The Catholics accepted, under the condition that they would continue to operate semi-independently, and that they would be a genuine co-equal, with none over them.
Due to the heavy influence of the Moralintern in the founding of 4 out of the 5 unifaiths, much Christian theology was integrated as universal statements of all 5 unifaiths. Specifically, the principles of the Imago Dei, and of Free Will, the two iron principles of the Galov originate from Protestant, but specifically the Moralintern's Evangelical theology (Which in of itself probably originated from Catholic theology). These once Christian values have been somewhat universalized across all 5 unifaiths.
But more importantly, the Moralists, in an alliance with the Catholics have also cemented another important value across all 5 of the unifaiths. A doctrine of radical epistemological humility. ("Priests must have humility.")
As the other expansionary power group (Alongside the Merchants), the Galov has also put a rule that they are not allowed to absorb splinter groups into the unifaith until they have accepted the principles of humility, human dignity (Imago Dei), and Free Wil.
The 5 Unifaiths are still the origin point for the Galov, though as the Galov has grown, its bureaucracy has increasingly become something new.

The Galov Bureaucracy:
Eventually, an alliance developed into a true organization, and the Galov itself began needing real bureaucracy. A thin one, at first, but it eventually grew with time. Seeking to distance itself from the demagoguery of previous democracies and delusions of previous bureaucracies, the Galov resorted to something novel; sortition. 80% of the Galov's legislative assembly are known as "civic-sortition seats". Essentially, anyone who finished their Galov civics education at any kind of Galov affiliated university was prone to have their name put in to a lottery, and to be drawn. The remaining 20% are "civilian-sortition seats", who are names drawn from various core worlds, collected from various databases. Made to enable continued connection with those on the ground. These civilian seats, while a minority, are very closely respected and watched by the remaining 80%, being seen as the voices of the common people. ("Bureaucrats must have sortition, or elections.")

The Millennium Mandate:
The Millennium Mandate is the name of a secret agenda held by the Christian Moralintern, the founder and often considered the "father" of the modern Galov.
