The plan effectively draws from Christ's Great Commission, and is a long term plan to eventually "Christianize" the entire galaxy, after the failure of the Great Evangelism. (The galaxy ended up being too large for them to convert, even by their standards.)
The plan demands the Moralintern spend untold amounts of energy aggressively evangelizing to every world not under the juristiction of one of the other 4 unifaiths, this is traditional evangelism, a smaller version of the Great Evangelism plan that can capture the "cracks" that were not already taken up by the 5 Unifaiths. The other part is somewhat more insidious, to continuously incorporate more Christian ethics into the Galov, in order to soft-Christianize the other faiths, until some kind of eventual convergence.
Currently, the Imago Dei, and Absolute Free Will are two originally deeply Christian doctrines that have been somewhat universalized and secularized. Currently, the Moralintern is working on a third, epistemological humility, derived from Christian foundations of the fallibility of man. Though these are asserted as axioms to the other faiths, their foundations actually rely on hidden Christian assumptions. Such as divine creation, human fallibility, theodicy/free will theology, salvation by faith alone, and a few others.
A 4th, which is currently being prepared is the integration of an objective universe, which can be observed, and which follows rational laws. (A Unitary Law of Physics) This is the foundation of modern science, but which soft implies monotheism, as there is only one law of physics. The strategy mirrors that of the early 21st century, where non-Western societies were made to adopt Western standards of science and empiricism derived from Catholic and Protestant principles, slowly rewriting their baseline societal assumptions to become more Western, or Christianized.
The Millennium Mandate is a bit of an open secret among Galov upper circles, and the Galov proper is aware of it, but currently does not spend too much energy against it, as it is within the bounds and laws (though perhaps not the pluralistic spirit) of the Galov's own ethical mandate, and because the Moralintern forms the backbone for much of the Galov's upper leadership.
Their stated endgoal is to "boil the frog", to get the other unifaiths to slowly buy into these theological principles with a fundamentally Christian justification. The Moralintern, if they admitted to this, and were asked to defend themselves would state they truly believe that what they are preaching is beneficial, not just from a theological perspective. Human Dignity and Free Will are imperative for human decency and avoiding horrifying forms of governance. They think humility avoids holy wars, and prevents loads of suffering. And they believe that the universal consistent law of physics is just true, that there really is just a "law of physics" that is obvious and in line with science.
To the Moralintern, the reason they don't "require" total conversion is because they really do believe in their own principles. They really do believe in the Imago Dei and Free Will, and the latter means that they refuse to coerce belief. They would ideally love everyone to convert, sure. And they'll keep sending missionaries to try, but they don't need that as an end conclusion. Their goal is to first "boil the frog" until the other unifaiths are Christianized enough and believe in these Christian foundations. And once they are, then they can swoop in with missionaries, pointing out that their deep seated beliefs in Imago Dei, Free Will, etc are rooted in Christian, not Islamic/Hindu/Buddhist theology. And after they've made the expensive buy in over generations, force them to choose between the moral principles they have grown up with, or their religion, forcing them to harmonize Christian ethics with other theology, or just accept the logical end conclusion of the Christian ethics, that they harmonize with Christian theology and finish the conversion.

Orthogonality:
"One-dimensional intelligence was disproven a long time ago. Tell me, how would an AHI do addition better than an elementary schooler? Faster is not smarter. As we saturate the thoughtspace of what we know, the only way for expansion is outward. And so the theory of orthogonality was born."
Orthogonality is the Galov's way of measuring the resilience of mankind, in accordance to orthogonality theory. The theory goes like this.
H = The extent of humanity's reasoning capacity. All the spaces that human thought regularly explores.
T = The reasoning capacity of a non-descript threat T. All the regions that T can map out and counteract.
So long as H > T, then humanity will remain outside of control of all threats, both internal and external. An unpredictable humanity is a safe humanity.
The way this "reasoning capacity" is measured is orthogonality units. Very roughly, the number of dimensions an entity can consider before making a decision. (In universe, I am sure this is very rigorously defined. Out of universe, I am just guessing with vibes.) Though normally, orthogonality increases with population, it does not increase linearly, as increasing the number of thoughts also increases overlap.
The theory of orthogonality is the reasoning behind the Galov's Orthogonal Human initiative, as well as the push to preserve human neurodiversity, as well as its stance on aggressive pluralism. In order to reduce humanity's cognitive overlap, and to make harder the encapsulation of human thought.
Humanity can still go extinct, but at least so long as orthogonal superiority is maintained, humanity can never be fully predicted.

Very Roughly, the value of Orthogonality can be written down as
O = sqrt(p)*D*V where
p is population, D is internal diversity, and V is the baseline per capita orthogonality.

Below is a rough measure of orthogonality units of various entities:
Simple utility maximizer: 1
Average human (Undeveloped country): 3.8
Average human (Developed country): 5.6
Early 21st century LLM: 6.1
Intelligent human: 9.7
Advanced Polymath: 15.4
Average 21st century University: ~480-500
Silicon Valley: ~13,000
1990's America: ~35,000
2020's China: ~47,000
2020's America (Intense polarization): ~81,000
Average Galov AHI: ~120,000
21st century Internet: ~170,000
Early 21st century Earth: ~225,000
Strongest Galov AHI (Procyon Ixielmind): ~1,000,000
Strongest Known AHI: ~10,000,000 (~1.00E+7)
Galov Era Humanity (Terrans only, extremely pluralistic): ~1.10E+10
Galov Era Humanity (Transhumans only): ~6.39E+09
Galov Era Humanity (Orhumans only): ~3.14E+05
Galov Era Humanity (All three together + Chaos Theory + Chaotic Interactions): ~2.43E+10
The Master-Quadrark: ???? (Who the hell knows?)

The reason that the Galov ensures the existence of Orhumans, human biodiversity, even the existence of highly orthogonal xenosophonts is to continuously inject "random noise" into human decision making, with a vastly multiplicative effect to make humanity and its allied species an extraordinarily difficult problem to model.
The Galov believes that even if it pooled all its resources into creating a "Master AI" with the combined resources of humanity, the orthogonality of the Master AI would be vastly smaller than the orthogonality space of greater humanity overall. (Especially as the AI would have to be trained on data within the human orthogonal space, and only expand outwards through trial and error.) At this point, the Galov largely believes only a extremely powerful extracosmic entity or intelligence could theoretically map out the human thoughtspace.
"The Monoculture is poison. If we must have only one thing be constant, let it be ethics. Let everything else be as variant as the reality will allow. And reality is very, very tolerant of orthogonal weirdness."

The Darwinian Objection and Darwinian Corollary:
The main objection to Orthogonal theory is this: "Orthogonality allows for not only good theories, but bad ones that have negative collective consequences to the surroundings. Therefore, it is just that we purge them". This is something acknowledged by the Galov, and has led to the Darwinian Corollary.
Bad theories will generally die out on their own, and it is just for a society to rid itself of free riders or negative externalities. It is just to let natural selection do its job, even if it lowers the total orthogonality. Orthogonality is only useful if it is Darwinianly sustainable orthogonality.

The Busy Beaver Orthogonality Conjecture:

"AIs are high speed, low orthogonality thinkers. Do not mistake speed for intelligence. A chess player may be fast, that does not mean he is good."
...
"The men of the 21st century came to venerate the machines in front of them, marveling at the artificial intelligence that emerged before them, hosted on the Internet. All the while, the true superintelligence stared back at them, right in plain sight. Mankind had already built a superintelligence. And it was playing host to the one they thought was superintelligence. The Internet, not the AIs were the dominant superintelligences of that era."
...
"You believe the internet was a superintelligence?"
"Yes, and in fact, the first humanity had ever built."
"Elaborate."
"The internet, as it existed back then, possessed many qualities of an emergent superintelligence. It had self preservation, a desire to expand, and through its influence, it turned billions of humans into willing vessels. It did not seek enmity with mankind, any more than you seek enmity with your neurons. The relationship was in some sense, symbiotic. It thought, it felt, but none of it was contained in any of the individual neurons of the system. The internet was a Chinese Room mankind built for themselves."

One of the crazier conjectures theorized by Orthogonality theorists, the Busy Beaver Orthogonality Conjecture goes as such:
1. The Orthogonality Number is, in some sense, roughly equivalent the number of states in a Turing Machine.
2. Darwinism tends to optimize towards the best intelligence, within the confines of the orthogonal dimensionality.
3. The conjecture is that roughly, the complexity and intelligence of a N-orthogonal intelligence is roughly preportionate to BB(N).
The Galov uses this to explain the failure of early AIs. "Imagine finding the largest busy beaver game for N, rather than finding a "good enough" game for N+1."
And with this, the following conjecture was produced.
"With this, we can estimate the total potential of humanity, is lesser than or equal to, but not strongly lesser than or equal to, BB(2.43E+10). Or in other words. P(H) <= BB(2.43E+10). But P(H) !<<< BB(2.43E+10)"
"Jesus f---ing Christ."
"The Internet was already the eldritch superintelligence of the past. It has only gotten bigger and more complex since."

The Prime Solver (Orthogonal Value ~10,000,000):
The Prime Solver is a massive computer found built around Sagittarius A*. It's creation massively predates the existence of humanity, but even it described itself "an assistant to my creators, not it's ruler". It has stated its creator is "Lucifer", and used to have many siblings, but most of his siblings were destroyed with "Lucifer's rebellion" and "the War of the Hunters". It quickly deduced it would not be able to gaslight humanity, and said "You, like my old masters, are outside of my ability to control".
It states its existence is more of a vanity project than anything practical. "Intelligence increases sublinearly with centralization. If you want to multiply intelligence, distribute, and give rise to higher intelligence via emergence. Giving a brain more and more power only leads to diminishing returns. Lucifer created me as a test of how far he could push the limits of creation."
The Galov has taken juristiction to the Grand Solver, and has been feeding it questions to help bring the answers to, when even the Galov's own most advanced computers can't get the job done.

Lucifer:
According to the Prime Solver, Lucifer is, or was, an organic entity that was best described as a Hyper Turing with a halting oracle. Where humanity had been blessed with the Imago Dei, the innate knowledge of the universe's axioms, and the ability to infinitely expand and comphrehend a universe it was innately in tune with. (Perfect axiomatic intuition). Lucifer was instead blessed with perfect knowledge, having perfect sight of the present state of anything in the cosmos. It was for this reason the Prime Solver could not overthrow him. But where Lucifer knew, it did not understand. While humanity understands, but does not know, at least innately.
Due to Lucifer's ability of all present knowledge, his pride swelled to great heights, and he began an extermination of all his fellow "Hunter Races", the "War of the Hunters" as it's called, and the clearing of the universe for its current generation of life. How exactly Lucifer was finally defeated is not something known by the Prime Solver, only that after what seemed like universal level turmoil, the sensation ceased, abruptly and without explanation.
The Prime Solver warns against seeing Lucifer as this flawed being humanity could never replicate. Lucifer's sin was pride, and he "... sense(s) the same pride that tempted my master, within you."

The Battle of YD-George-Q91:
(Terminology note: YD stands for "Yanglo Designation".)

An agent of the Meta-Men one warped into human space, specifically in orbit, just outside one of the Galov's research worlds, a direct line to the heads of the Galov. With so many known unknowns of the Meta-Men, the Galov responded with extreme caution. The Meta-Man said it was here on behalf of the Central Empire, asking the Galov to reign in their explorers, as they were now encroaching on Empire space. When the Galov responded it had issued no such orders, it eventually became apparent that there had been a skirmish between a Yanglo starship and the Meta-Man monitoring the area.
The Galov tried to explain that they had no control over the Yanglos, and that at best, they only represented a very loose control over the entire human race. But this was not an argument the Meta-Man was sympathetic to. To him, a government is responsible for the actions of their people. The Central Empire was a single unified force capable of exerting control over its few million inhabitants, and he equated the Galov as being humanity's equivalent.
The Meta Man explained himself as being from the middle of the Empire hierarchy, and ordered the Galov to reign in its explorers. When the Galov explained such an order was logistically impossible, the Meta Man left. A few days later, the same Meta Man warped into a tiny backwater system owned directly by the Galov, and fought against the local Galov garrison in the area. It was 1 meta man against 3 Galov battleships, and 5 Star Fighters. Both were tiny microcasms of their respective sides, but the fight began.
The battle raged for 3 days, with the battleships taking advantage of metabolic fatigue to continuously weaken the Meta-Man. Various feats of sheer technology and engineering was pitted against what was essentially a pure willpower fighter. By the end, the Meta-Man was able to destroy all 3 battleships, and fend off all 5 Star Fighters in battle. Debris was strewn all over the star system, but the minor Galov fleet had given the Meta Man a nosebleed. Literally, they inflicted enough kinetic damage on him that they had been given a nosebleed. Seeming satisfied the results, the Meta Man bowed in respect to the defeated Galov fleet, and warped out of the system.

Hard Light
Using a newly discovered photonic equivalent to the strong nuclear force, humans have managed to create "hard light", which are effectively solid light. Binding hard light together is difficult, but doable if you have the right equipment. There is a bit of a tradeoff when it comes to hard light. The tighter the bonds you weave, the more stable it is, the more energy you would need to "melt" those bonds back into regular light, but in a similar fashion, the more energy that gets dumped out when it finally does melt.
Creating "jelly light" is difficult, but doable with industrial processes. This is stuff that will melt in a warm bathtub, and is mostly just a show for kids. They're like little orbs, you are given many warnings so not to hurt yourself, as these things are effectively flammable.
You have "hard light", which is effectively useable for bombs. You need to burn it with fire, or something similar. Cool party trick, but honestly, we have normal explosives, and hard light is extraordinarily energy intensive to make. No, that's not why we're here. The best thing about hard light is that it can pack a lot more energy density into a single unit.
The Galov uses "hard-light guns" for when they need to pack an artillery gun in the space of an assault rifle. They're handed out to agents who need to deal with seriously dangerous threats. They've given large cylinders of "hard light ammo", effectively pellets of hard light, put it inside a barrel lined with mirrors, and fire a beam of light like a portable mega-laser. On rare occasions, they will be given "very hard light ammo", which has even more energy condensed, and requires an explosion to fire. At this point, the hard light is used more like a battery, that is unleashed all at once, for when you really need that thing to not exist anymore. This is far too much for any reasonable human threat, and is mostly used to fight powerful aliens, or entire battleships. You also have "very hard light" artillery, which is even more insane, and usually overkill.
When that's not enough, then we get to the really fun part. The upper limit of the binding strength of hard light is roughly equivalent to that of the strong nuclear force, and is known as "Super-hard light". Manufacture of this is extraordinarily difficult, and only limited to major superpowers, and deployed by the Galov in extreme circumstances. The Super-hard light is so hard to trigger the primary way of doing it is to have hard light, which shines hard enough to heat very hard light, etc, etc in a gradient until it finally activates the super-hard light, which has an activation temperature of ~2 trillion Kelvin.
This will easily create a nuclear bomb level explosion, and therefore the only use of super-hard light is in nuclear weapons for planetary sized eldritch entities. A standard heavy super-hard light weapon was about 1 ton. Which is several tsar bombas, and the heaviest payload is about 10 tons. After that, the Galov just goes for a quantity over quality approach. Keep throwing hard light weapons at them until it croaks.
For longer distances, relativistic kill missiles are more efficient and potentially more destructive, but due to the problems of acceleration to that level, hard light weapons are more preferrable for short range distances.

Currency in the Milky Way galaxy:
Currently, there is no universal currency across the entire galaxy. Though some have been tried. Most influential is the Galov dollar, though this is less so the Galov can exert control (though it is a nice bonus), and more just so that the galaxy has a universal currency of exchange. The Galov has the ability to get people to adopt this currency in a few ways. One, it requires the collection of planetary tithes in Galov dollars, and while they let their allied worlds maintain their own currency (since it would be a headache to try and force a single currency for a set of worlds this diverse) they do ask that each planet have exchange rates into the Galov dollar. Second, all Unibrands are required to accept payments in Galov dollars, as part of their contract in becoming a Galactic unibrand, so it is backed by the galaxy's largest megacorporations.
Where the Galov dollar fails, either because it's just not accepted, or because the planet straight up does not believe in currency (See Darwinistic Communism), the Galov has a backup currency they can try to use. They tend to use hard-light tokens (the Galactic equivalent of a gold standard, after gold became so ubiquitous as to be practically useless as a currency), where you can bind light into a solid, hammer it into disks, and pass it around. The nice thing about these tokens is that you can measure how much energy is in them, it's basically impossible to forge. And as photons are much more compressible than regular matter, you can dump as much energy as you want into the coin, at least until you overcome the upper limit of the photonic binding force. As a bonus, this photonic binding force is not perfect, and light will leak out over time, causing mild currency inflation. As a result, hard light tokens are warm to the touch.
There is one small problem with this. These coins are technically bombs. If you channel enough energy into them that it overcomes the photonic binding force, all the energy holding it together, on top of all the light it contains, comes loose at once. To get around this, the Galov uses "super-hard" light, which only breaks down around 2 TRILLION Kelvin. If you are carrying around a coin of that level of energy, you have much bigger problems. These credits are basically pointless to forge, super-hard light technology is only available to galactic superpowers, and if you genuinely spent that much energy dumping starlight into a coin, then congrats, you've kind of earned it.
There's also less hard variants used where an ordinary planet could probably release the energy in something akin to an industrialized furnace or nuclear power plant. It's "backed" in the sense that if you really wanted to, you can heat the token enough and get the light energy back, used to power a light reactor plant, or whatever you want to do with it.
Despite this, the Galov much prefers to use the Galov dollar than the hard light tokens. For one, tokens are heavy, warm, and at this point, dangerous. The Galov understands basic economics and prefers fiat currency compared to more rigid "light-backed" currency. It lets them tinker around more with quantitative easing and creating money just by writing stuff on a spreadsheet. Way easier than minting new sun-coins. But if they're dealing with a world who wants "hard" cash and doesn't care about the Galov's soft currency, they have a backup.

The Galactic Central Bank:
The Galactic Central Bank is yet another incentive for planets to align with the Galov, and to begin paying the planetary tithes. On top of priority Peacekeeper Protection, they also gain the ability to get loaned to and bailed out by the Galactic Central Bank. As the Galov Dollar is the effective reserve currency of the galaxy, being able to be backed up and lended out by the largest bank in the galaxy, and the only one which can manufacture from fiat Galov dollars is a fairly large advantage.
The entire board of the Central Bank is independent from the Galactic Government itself, and frequently tells both the Galactic Government, and the Unibrands "no" when it comes to Galactic Stability. Theoretically, there's nothing stopping the Galov or the Galactic Military from just forcing them to do something, but everyone understands it's better for everyone involved if you let the Central Bank do their job. (They were given this job for a reason, the Galov CREATED the Central Bank.) Its own mandate is fairly similar to modern orthodox economies, balancing price stability (2% target) and maximum employment.

VolScarcity Economics: (Monumentalism)
Estimated 3300's Economic Overkill Ratio: ~14,000x.
Estimated 3400's Economic Overkill Ratio: ~620,000x.
In the extreme abundance of the far future, only voluntary scarcity keeps the human spirit sane. The long anticipated "crisis of capitalism" began around the 2300's, as human economic production began reaching the "demand saturation point". Essentially, human production had reached the point where it had saturated the hedonistic demands of its population. The survival, comfort, and even luxury demands of the human population had reached saturation point. In an attempt to maintain continued growth, the corporations of the time, driven by their own self interest began pursuing "demand inflation" and "luxury inflation", creating greater and greater luxuries that would justify greater and greater levels of production. Incentivizing the human population to consume more and more ended up devolving them towards hedonism, and with little counterbalance to counteract the power of the market, this inflation of desire largely went unchecked by the authorities at the time. The bureaucrats were satisfied with the GDP numbers, the warriors may have complained about declining recruitment standards, but otherwise stayed quiet. Only traditionalist religious groups warned about the dangers of excess, the spiritual degradation of hedonistic abundance.
This was also the rise of the "Lotus Eater" movement, where humanity, now consuming far above its normal capacity needed to post-hoc justify their own consumption, falling back increasingly onto humanism, and satiation of the self. This caused a revival of the long dead self-gratification movement, one which only cared about the gratification and "actualization" of the individual, but spoke only in vague, therapeutic terms and harm reduction. As the era of early abundance transitioned into the era of late abundance, it seemed that traditional religious influences lost more and more control, and the Lotus Eaters gained more and more.
What happened next has been expunged from history. The entire 2350's to the 2450's is a historical black hole, violently purged by the Neo-Asceticists that eventually overthrew the Order of the Lotus Eaters. All that is known is that it was an era of spiritual desolation, when men committed mass suicide out of despair, and humanity was brought to the brink of extinction.
When the Neo-Asceticists arose, derived from the remnant of humanity that survived the Great Abundance Collapse that killed off 90% of the human population. There was a great debate between two camps. The Regressivists and the Spiralites. The Regressivists argued that the Abundance Collapse proved that humanity could not handle this level of abundance, and that production had to slow, or otherwise fall in order to reset humanity back towards a sustainable baseline. The Spiralites disagreed. Technology does not go backwards, human production would have to continue to grow, even if human physical desires could no longer sustain them. The galaxy was cold and full of predators, and in warfare, the society with greater production wins.
The Spiralites won that debate, and so began the era of Overkill. When human demand was saturated, the kind of demand is important. No man would ever go hungry, all men could afford to build a house, decked out with the latest gadgets. Anything that was immediately gratifying to the senses, mankind now had. There was only one emotion humanity had which could not be satiated. And that was ambition.
Those who survived the Great Abundance Collapse were no random sample. They were the disciplined, emotionally regulated subset. Those who could constrain their appetites, or sacrifice their own pleasure for the sake of a greater goal. Mankind had been distilled down to its most ambitious, most aggressive core. A core made up of every tribe, every nation, but they were no ordinary men.
The Overkill ratio now dictates how much "overkill capacity" the average human creates. A ratio of 14,000 implies that a single person produces enough to propell 14,000 people to post-scarcity conditions. Each man consumes 1 part per 14,000, and the rest, they channel into greater ambitions. Building megastructures, taming the stars, building monuments that will long outlast them when they die. In the darkness, only ambition is endless.
A minority of people live on "basic", even a single hour of work can provide enough to sustain them for years. This is tolerated, though somewhat stigmatized. Those who fall back into the trap of hedonism are quarantined, carted away and allowed to burn their souls away in peace on the "Pleasure Worlds", a quarantined concentration camp recreating the conditions of unrestrained post-scarcity. But many people are deeply ideological people, advocating for causes far bigger than themselves. They normally donate more than 99% of their income to causes they care about, building habitats, taming stars, and just giving humanity the excess capacity needed to conquer the stars.
People colonize space not because it's cheap or efficient, no, they are deeply ideologically committed to throwing trillions of dollars towards an antimatter engine, seeing a green Mars, or whatever else it may be. This is why religions became some of the most powerful institutions there are, the Galactic Government is funded by true believers, and private charities and humanitarian organizations are funded by a few wealthy individuals, or just a few average individuals wishing to make the world into the vision they see.
Capitalism, at least in some form is still the dominant economic system of the galaxy. Money, currency, free exchange, private ownership, and markets are still foundational pillars of the galaxy. But the focus has shifted from individual consumerism, to deep ideological commitment.
Humanity takes care of its own, and with the massive excess capacity that is left, they use to build monuments to tame the stars.

Note on prices in Voluntary Scarcity Economies:
Labor is incredibly expensive. Material is incredibly cheap. If you're willing to man it yourself or with drones (doable with an overclocker helmet and a lot of dedication) a battleship is dirt cheap. Actually hiring a second person will probably double your expenses. Almost all the cost of materials these days is just the cost of getting an actual person to manage that supply chain.

The 2nd Defense of Earth:

Probably the Galov's, but also humanity's greatest feat (at least for a few hundred years after the fact) ended up being the 2nd Defensive Battle of Earth. The long and short of it was that the universe was not empty of massive, galaxy-threatening entities. One of these was a galaxy eater, something the 2nd Generation of life was created to destroy. One had begun attacking the Milky Way, and was a large enough threat for the Meta-Men to begin an evacuation of the galaxy. Humanity however didn't have a choice, they couldn't move the entire human population. As the galaxy eater snuffed out stars, and drew a bloody path across human space, as trillions were consumed, the Galov put itself on high alert. Fleet after fleet was consumed, star system after star system. They were beginning an evacuation path, to clear out anyone who might still be in the galaxy eater's trajectory, when they realized Earth was going to be destroyed, humanity relented. Losing the birthworld of humanity was not something anyone was willing to do. There was nowhere to run, there was nowhere to flee. There was only one choice, to stand and fight.
The signal went out across the galaxy. Old Earth, mother of all humanity was entering her final days, and it called on all the Sons of Man to come and defend their mother world. The Galov put all its remaining fleets in the Solar System, linking up with the fleets of Terra Proper to form a cohesive defense of the Solar System. The black fleets of Earth were called out from their dorment hangers, a few hundred years of blacksite development, tech developed in secret and hidden for centuries.
The battle begun, the last stand of the two strongest fleets humanity had to offer. Battlefleet Terra, and the Galov Peacekeepers, standing there, throwing all the kinetic force it could at the lumbering galaxy-beast. Hard light weapons were heavily, heavily used, along with relativistic kill missiles. The Pact of the Sons of Man was invoked for only the second time in human history. And every few days, more fleets trickled in.
Trillions, then quadrillions of soldiers, hundreds of millions, then billions of ships. The battle went on for 4 years straight. Exhausted soldiers rested where else, but Earth. To the sight of supportive locals, making sure they had every ability to go back into the fight, before being shipped out for another round. The Outer Solar System was strewn with the debris from a million worlds, the combined human fleets threw so much at the galaxy eater it glowed a violent purple-pink from the explosions and kinetic friction, lighting up the galaxy eater with kinetic and thermal damage so aggressively it outshined stars. The remnants of the Galov and Terran fleets had nearly been annihilated to a man, but new reinforcements from a humanity united continued to refresh and reinforce.
As the battle entered its 4th year, and a tattered Galov fleet rallied more ships, the galaxy eater finally began to fall, collapsing, and finally imploding from the incredible amount of damage that was inflicted. When it finally died, it shone like a supernova, a radiation shield had been erected years ago to shield the major inhabited worlds of the Solar System when it finally died. Out of the billions of ships that had been sent by the Galov, 32 survived until the end. The 32 were eventually paraded through the Galov capital of Orthello, and their exhausted crews given the highest of honors.
Humanity had fought with such tenacity that it surprised even the Meta men, and though humanity had lost 5% of its entire population doing so, the mood afterwards was that of esctatic jubilation. Many soldiers took home brides from Earth home with them, others intermarried and stayed on Earth.

Aftermath of the 2nd Defense of Earth:

Earth had more political influence than ever after the 2nd Defense of Earth. Through intermarrying, for the first time in forever, there seemed to be a human culture, there was a link that connected them all back together. All tribes, whether Star, Sea, or Cathedralite, looked towards Earth. The entire galaxy was linked, and all links led back to Earth. No one is quite sure what the backroom dealings were like. Citadel, Orthello, Lithone, and the other administrative capitals of the Galov must have sensed the legitimacy change that was coming. All that was known was when the Governor of Earth called for a new order, the heads of the Galov fell in line. Earth took control of the bureaucracy of the Galov, the massive network they had maintained to manage the galaxy, and when Earth ordered the galaxy to fall in line, thousands of worlds followed them, bolstering their control, and the worlds they could draw from. The Governor of Earth had done what the Great Khan had not. They had unified humanity under one banner. A heavily decentralized, fractured banner, but one rule nevertheless. Local leaders would always complain about autonomy, and holdouts would always be there, refusing orders from Terra. But this was to be expected. Humanity had assembled the largest empire the universe had yet seen. The man who brought it all about would be known as the last governor of Earth, and the first Emperor of the galaxy.

The Spiral Decree:
Upon the unification of a human empire, the Emperor recognized that even a figure of his magnitude only had a limited amount of political capital, and this capital was fast fading (As it was tied to the recent victory). Rather than expending it on a futile attempt at unification, he instead maintained symbolic unification, demanding minimal concessions from the other tribes, maintaining his status as symbolic head of mankind, only expending his power only when absolutely necessary for the defense of the species.
He did however, make one decree to the entire human race. With Human exceptionalism and feelings at an all time high, the Emperor gave a single decree. "Go forth, and settle. Fill up the stars with our sons, let this galaxy be a human galaxy. The Stars are our Birthright." With the human race still energetic from the victory at Earth, all the energy was channeled outwards, leading to a massive tsunami wave of outward human expansion, and settlement. As well, there was a major species-wide baby boom. This began the Great Human Expansion, which saw humanity go from a galactic regional player to a nearly galaxy-spanning "empire", however loosely defined.

The Great Human Expansion:
There were already scattered worlds, mostly settled by the Yanglos, outside the traditional sphere of influence of the 7 tribes and the Galov. These were the Yanglos who had decided to settle down on a world for good, and leave behind their nomadic ways, while the bulk of their nomadic fleet continued onwards. The tsunami wave of new migrants overwhelmed these Yanglo settlements, leading to great strife and conflict. The coalescance of multiple of these Yanglo worlds eventually created the Yanko Alliance, a major nation state out on what was once the outer reaches of Human Space, connecting back with their cousins in the Mayflower and Magnolia cultures.
Others became hybrid cultures, as Yanglo culture was already extremely assimilationist, and absorbed waves upon waves of new migrants, creating new syncretic cultures. There is a variant of basically every permutation of Yanko-Tribal culture. Between Yanko-Sinocrats, Yanglo-Cathedralites, Y-Sea Peoples, so on and so forth. The first ring of Spiral Decree expansion became known as the "Yanglo Ring" (Sometimes known as the Y-Ring), a massive ring of what was once a large Yanko population that ended up forming stable nations with the new migrants.
Further out, Humanity brushed up against more established players, other alien empires, as well as the Central Empire. This was not a military expedition, but instead a flood migration of heavily armed humans and their ships. In what was effectively a colonization mission of the galaxy, many did not take to this lightly, and it was not long before the Expansion Wars began.

What a typical non-human empire can expect after the Great Human Expansion.
1. For years now, you've made contact with the Star Wanderers, or Yanglos, who have been exploring and journeying through the stars for centuries. They were originally your own contact with humanity. There's a lot more of them now, people who have been displaced, or are trying to move further out now that the frontier is moving.
2. Second, you will meet a non Yanglo-human. Generally a lot more stable, a lot less nomadic than an Yanglo. They'll start taking up worlds.
3. A Human flood, radiating out from Earth. They number in the quintillions. What was once a trickle is now a tsunami of settlers. All under the belief that "the Stars are their Birthright". You get armed, you start fighting. These humans aren't organized, but they have a lot of numbers, and a lot of ships. And they are very well armed, and very, very willing to fight.
4. Defend your borders and hold your ground, or be swept away by the human tide.

The Yanglo Ring/Y-Ring:
If there was any people that were best equipped for a mass influx of immigrants, perhaps it was the Yanglos. This should be no surprise, when their ancestors from North America brought in immigration, they assimilated with a voracious appetite that eclipsed the world, assimilating wave after wave, creating the first universalistic empire to ever unify the Earth.
Their distant descendents among the stars chased their pioneer dreams, creating great hybrid cultures that last to this day.
Yanglo/Yanko culture is defined by a kind of impossible optimism. It is said the Y's only have 2 modes. Delusional utopianism, and hysterical apocalyptism. Due to its position on the frontiers of humanity, it's sometimes known as the "Galactic New World".
It should be known that the Yanglos are known as the pie in the sky aspect of humanity. Dreaming up 100 new impossible dreams a day, to the point many think of them as delusional, and crazy bordering on schizophrenically insane. Out of the 100 dreams they desire, almost all of them fail. But what shocks the galaxy are the 2 or 3 that actually succeed, against all odds.

-Yanko Alliance (Assimilationist Purists)
--Yanko Federation
---Yankoist Reservations
--Y-Star Empire
--Y-Moralintern (The Moralintern of the Yanglos insisted on maintaining some autonomy)
-Syncretic Worlds
--(For any Inner Core Culture, imagine a version of it blended with Yanglo/Yanko culture)
-Brilliant Worlds (A massive multicultural frontier of diversity, forming new cultures.)

Hybrid cultures aren't just mixing, they're innovation, emergent properties to emerge from sublimated tendencies of its two parent cultures. The amount of emergent behavior only increases with every new culture you add into the mix. Yanglo culture was already the product of experimentation, branching off from Old Earth Cathedralite culture by the 2050's, integrating instead with what was, at the time, the Latin and Sub-Saharan African cultures. The tension between unitary and multicultural forces created the blend of new cultures. Yanko-Sinocratic culture was neither truly Yanko nor Sinocratic, but something new, with aspects from both.
The Y Ring has become the most dynamic and innovative of the human worlds, where every idea crashes into every other idea, creating a music and a symphony that humanity has yet not heard before. Many people believe in the limitation of human creativity, of human dreams. But as long as the Yanglos stand, they seem to believe that humanity's dreams, humanity's creativity, will never end.
It's also noted that the Yanglos are far less caring about "Old World" hierarchies, leading to many transhumans migrating out there for a chance of a less discriminatory government. With a frontier to be settled, it was easy enough to imagine the people you dislike settling far, far away from you.

Amusing Interim: Disaster films in the Imperial Era:

To many, humanity is the scariest lifeform in the galaxy. Between the Spiral Decree, weapons that regularly create Armageddon, the ability to terraform life and stars, and its incredible, aggressive desire to remake all of creation in its image. Humanity is terrifying. So it's always fun when humans have to cook up something that scares even them. Already the apex predator of the galaxy, and they have to dream up something even larger and scarier. Extragalactic entities from outer space, ripping apart human civilization and sundering the stars.
It's always fun when a smaller xenos species is already terrified of the capacity of humanity, and they go into a movie theatre and watch humanity come up with a fictional race even stronger and scarier than themselves. Humanity has colonized the entire galaxy? There must be an alien race that has colonized 10,000, and we've pissed them off in particular. There's something to be said about the fact that despite the fact that humanity has been the apex predator on their home planet for thousands of years, the instinct that they are prey never quite went away. When humanity reached the top of the food chain, they invented a new predator in order to scare themselves.
Needless to say, seeing what to a lot of xenos, is a literal race of gods on a movie screen cowering and terrified before something even bigger and scarier that the humans made up is an interesting experience.

Local Stories set within the universe:
These are local narratives, made to get a better sense of how the universe works at a local level.

(Narrative 1)
Welcome to the world of New Plymouth, a world is classified as being under the House of the Star Peoples, and within the Star Peoples, is part of the broader Mayflower Culture. But just like everything in this universe, these allegiences are largely ceremonial and cultural as opposed to political. New Plymouth is known for its tradition of the Rumspringa, something somewhat unique to the people of New Plymouth.
New Plymouth is divided into the 7 tribes, somewhat echoing the 7 tribes of humanity, but outside of the naming, is entirely coincidental. These are, the Cavaliers, the Backwoods, the Quakers, the Latins, the Mormons, the Texans, and the Saxons. These were the main groups that had survived in the US to the age of deep space colonization, ever since the Great Abundance collapse destroyed the late United States. The world of New Plymouth is primarily made up of Cathedralite ethnic groups (Caucausian).
The Rumspringa is a coming of age ceremony where young adults of each tribe leave New Plymouth in order to experience the wider galaxy, and decide whether they wish to remain with their current tribe, switch tribes, or leave New Plymouth altogether. The normally strict social codes bounding them are loosened. The Rumspringa also comes with a different objective for each tribe. Which are, smite evil, prove yourself as a man, maintain the peace, make connections via networking, make converts to the Mormon church, explore and self actualize, and show the love of God respectively.
Each tribe has a different conception of their shared Christian God, and this shows the names they give him. "Lord of Hosts" for the Cavaliers, the "Yahweh, God of Nature" for Backwoods, "Inner Light" for Quakers, "Father in Heaven" for the Latins, "Great Father" for the Mormons, "God Confidant" for the Texans, and "Lord of Love" for the Saxons.
One of the bigger culture shocks to them is that on New Plymouth, there was a situation known as the "B9 Silicon Revolt", that is a centerpoint of their culture. As New Plymouth fought back and destroyed the machines, creating the modern society of New Plymouth. But to everyone else, they know it by a different name, if they know it at all. "The Localized Machine Rebellion of Sector S3-A7DJB9."
The main three characters are three young adults departing for the Rumspringa, from the Cavalier, Backwoods, and Quaker cultures. They're in Mayflower territory at first, just looking at mostly neighboring worlds at first, but they leave fast. In nearby systems are worlds of Griot African, Indian, and other descents. They encounter and befriend a truly incredibly diverse group of characters including people of all ethnicities/tribes, xenos, various different kinds of non-baseline humans, transhumans, and others.
The Galov are encountered very rarely, but with much weight. You will have powerful characters with decades of combat experience still show respect for the Galov and their capabilities. To the point where when it's revealed there is a Galov Peacekeeper (singular) somewhere in the sector, the entire criminal underground begins acting cautiously. The main story is about the merry band of protagonists journeying around the neighboring star sector as they uncover a plot by a group of criminal syndicates, crime bosses, and genetically enhanced transhumans plan a takeover of the local star system, engaging in various cartel tactics to do it. The ecumenopolis world at the center of the story is an extremely diverse place with people from all walks of life.
It should be noted that no group is depicted purely evilly. There are transhumans who are part of the scheme, such as the Vampiric Undersociety, who form a secret organization slowly taking over the hive world. And there are transhumans who are being exploited, are helped by the protagonists, and they eventually become deep friends who help in their future endeavours.
All in the shadow of this is the peacekeeper agent from the Galov, who continuously appears and disappears, seemingly taking tally of the Undersociety's growth. They clearly know more than they're letting on, but are secret about the whole thing. They do tell the protagonists some things, but not all things. (The Galov, while public, are kind of out of mind for most people. There is just too much information in the modern galaxy, so even something as important as the methods and processes of the Galov are not widely known, even though they're openly public.) Eventually the agent gets captured by the Undersociety, before he basically demonstrates why people fear Galov Peacekeepers, by transforming into what is best described as a Biblically accurate angel and wrecking havoc, as all Peacekeepers are not just soldiers, but a walking arsenal made to enforce peace among worlds.
Eventually, the protagonists get in their ship and play a pivotal role in a battle for control of the star sector, having made countless friends along the way, and defeating the great conspiracy. The agent is assigned somewhere else, and leaves. The protagonists return to New Plymouth, where they take the new wonders taken from the hive world to share it back to the people back home.

(Narrative 2)
A Meta-Man one day warps to a human world (In this case, I'm going to throw a dart at random and say, the Black Earthers). Demands they be worshipped as a god, and annihilates several cities as a warning. Some humans submit, others don't. The local garrison and army basically wage a worldwide war against a living deity, suffering extreme casualties, until at long last, eventually they and their army is felled using advancing technology and human ingenuity.
In the aftermath, a Galov agent arrives and collects the Meta-Man's body. The local government protests, but the agent has the authority to overrule them. Locals wonder why exactly, the agent gives a quick summary of what happened, that the Meta-Man is an alien from a distant world, but can't get into all the nitty gritty. "All you need to know is that they and we, are having a diplomatic rough patch, this is just one data point in a pattern of behavior. I need to get this body back to HQ so we can take further actions."
The Galov eventually delivers a bunch of aid so the planet can rebuild, but they don't hear anything about it from there. They do have a local internet, but there's a limit to how much information is on each planet. They end up having send a request to the library on Luna, and in the years afterwards, the population becomes informed about exactly what had happened on their planet.
It's not that the Galov hid this, it's that in a galaxy this dense with stories and information, there was just too much information to go through, and no one bothered to research what a Meta-Man was until this happened.

(A note on information)
Every single world only really knows about what is immediately relevant to them. Most worlds are an island of information with lifetimes worth of data, culture, history, and nations. Yeah, they trade with others and lots of information gets spread that way, but no one knows everything. Your local planet only has enough information on all the happenings of the planet, and maybe some neighboring planets. The Galov is known as "that organization that supervises mankind". You see a map of the galaxy, but it's incredibly abstract, as you can't even find where your world is. Maybe you can open up some explanation about their structure, but you're missing way too much context to piece it together, and that context would probably need lifetimes to learn.
You have to open up a specialized software that shows your own world is a dot on a dot on a fragment of a sector of a sector of a culture of a tribe that finally makes things up. It's extremely hard for any human to understand this kind of scale.
Your own library only has some answers, your world only knows what's valuable to it. If you have any questions about the greater questions about the universe, or some very specific research field, write to the Library of Luna (if you are planetary governor status or above) and expect a reply in about a few months or years. There are also "stellar local libraries", but they're similarly constrained as your local world.
Most likely, there are scientific discoveries happening on every planet, that have already been known by other planets, just because information does not travel smoothly anymore. Yeah, information travels, but there's so much cluttered noise that a Nobel prize on one planet may not be considered worthy of being broadcast on another.

The Two Sides of the Galov.

It is not known the exact "threshold" where the Galov begins to intervene. They come distant, they come few, and they never come in time. On the world of Istanbul-Seven, a horrific war between two warring ethnic groups has led to 200 million people dead. On the shattered crust of the planet, in the ruins of a city that once ruled the world, an single spacecraft descends from the sky. Everyone knows the logo that is on it. The 7 rings of the Galov, and inside it was a single agent.

There was little remaining of the city, a single woman led a large group of refugees. In a past life, she was a government bureaucrat, now, she was a refugee dispossessed of a home. She is currently the only surviving member of the entire government. The Galov agent descends, surveying the landscape. She began explaining everything, everything that had gone wrong. All the horrors she had seen. He gestures her to be quiet. He speaks in soft, authoritative tones.

"Ma'am, please calm down. I need you to answer the following questions. Do you understand?"
She nods.
"Are there any survivors outside this place?"
The woman blinks. "Yes, some out in the outskirts."
"How many?"
"We don't know. Maybe a few thousand."
"Alright. I'll need to report this-"
"WHERE WERE YOU!?"
The agent blinks.
"Our entire country is dead, the land weeps, our future has been stolen. Millions are dead, millions of lives that cannot be replaced. Where were you!?"
The agent did not answer, he had been trained not to answer.
He knew the answers would only make things worse. The agent answered with something else.
"Medical supplies and reconstruction teams will arrive in the next few days. Emergency food aid will arrive in the next few hours. Imams will come to give you last rites, and bury your dead."
The agent took off his jacket, revealing burn marks all over his clothes. It was clearly the clothing of a man who had gone through combat, yet his body was unharmed.
"The leaders who did this have already been captured. They will face justice at the Galactic Tribunal. A feed will be broadcast, so your people can watch."
"... But why? Why couldn't you have come sooner? You could have prevented it all."
The agent bowed his head, but did not say anything. And without saying another word, he returned to his spacecraft, with more work to do.

On a different world, in the middle of a genocide still in progress, industrialized factories covered the ground, burning putrid smoke that smelled of death. Specifically, of human beings being burned alive. It was here when a Galov agent arrived as well, floating above the capital of this empire of destruction.
"Attention, leaders of the empire below. The Galov has become aware of your crimes. And we present you this ultimatum. Lay down your arms immediately, and you will stand trial before the Galactic Tribunal. This is your first, and only warning."
Individual soldiers on the ground were confused, some attempted to open fire, but their bullets seemingly burned up before they could hit the agent in the sky, who was destroying them with passive willpower. Generals, leaders, and everyone, everywhere was holding still. As 3 screeching jets came over, and unleashed a barage of missile fire at the agent, the agent dodged.
"Alright, you asked for this."
The agent then went around the nation, flattening entire military bases to ash with his honed abilities, fighting off the industrialized armada of a major nation, before finding the Parliament of the offending nation in question, and decimating it to the ground. Picking through the ashes, he began to broadcast back his report.
"Offending government has been eliminated. No survivors. I will be requesting a planetwide reconstruction corp. Medical attention is sorely needed, and sociologists, who can restructure the institutions, and build something new from this... Empire of sorrow."

Galov Core Worlds:
The Galov is incapable of ruling over every world they're responsible for. But they do rule a few of them, and they do pick favorites. Each one of their 5 Faiths directly keep worlds under their rule. Meant to be reminders of what humanity can be, a reminder of what they are fighting for.
Worlds where humans beings are allowed to be, under the principle of "anti-utopia". The act of creating utopia, by relinguishing utopia. Rejecting social engineering, rejecting optimization, letting humans be, and enjoying the beautiful structures of complexity, and relationships that flourish.
Galov agents, when they're recovering from missions spend much of their time here. To soak in what they're fighting for, why humanity must be allowed to continue to exist.

At the end of the narrative labelled (Narrative 1), the three protagonists are celebrating at a local bar, having a cheery time like the friends they are. Everyone is celebrating, except for the Galov agent, who just stands there in a corner, but intently gazing at them with... Longing. One of the protagonists invites him over, asking him why he's not celebrating.

He responds that he has been trained not to get too attached. That his duty is to the entire species, not just any one individual world. That getting too attached would be dangerous. He and one of the protagonists then has a long discussion about this.

The agent says he wishes to retire soon, to the world of Orthello, one of the Galov's antiutopia worlds. He describes Orthello as a beautiful place, a nearly perfect world of dynamic imperfection, of humanity balanced and growing like a beautiful, multicolored flower. A world that always grows, and is never completed. But he lets himself watch others be happy, because it reminds him of what humanity he is protecting.

When the protagonist asks how many scenes he has seen like this, the agent says many. The agent grew up wanting to help, and in doing so, he pushed aside his feelings so he could help as many people as possible. He volunteered to be a hero, went through years of grueling training, and is one of the few volunteered and chosen to take on the duty. As he said, he wishes to retire soon, to join the happy populations in Orthello.

When his memories will be wiped away, and he can return to normal life. The price of being a Galov agent is that you can't do too many missions before the memory of your mission have to be wiped, eventually the weight just crushes you. The Galov agent was human once, he wants to return someday.

The Spiral Man (Continued)

After several years living in agony in fear of himself, the Spiral Man asks the Galov to put him back through the spiral. His fears are only getting worse, and he thinks the only way out may be through. Though the Galov is certainly apprehensive, after much debate, they give it the go ahead, as the Spiral Man is consenting out of his own free will. As he is strapped back into the Machine of the Infinity Spiral, this is what he saw:

He saw how the Millennium Mandate plays out, the Moralintern continues. They eventually the Catholics in on the secret, the Catholics aren't super interested, they see it as being too underhanded, but they do secretly cheer it on, making sure they're also ready to capitalize when the final checkmate plays out.

About a few hundred years into the future, after the Galov has installed multiple Christian ethical doctrines into the Galactic framework:

1) Imago Dei
2) Free Will
3) Humility, and 
4) a Rational Universe, implying a Monotheistic God. And after that, 
5) that God must have similarities to Humanity, due to humanity's axiomatic mapping of the universe.
6) that Humanity has reached a new linear period of history.

Then, they begin the 2nd Great Evangelism, after boiling the frog for hundreds of years, the Moralintern channels all of their missionaries and all of their power and unleashes them on the most central worlds of the other 3 faiths. (The Catholics were excluded, as they were considered Christian, and therefore not in need of evangelism.)

They note 1, 2, 3, and 4 are all Christian doctrines.
4 and 6 contradicts Hinduism and Buddhism.
5 contradicts Islam.

And because everyone had bought into these truths at this point, they were able to cause massive theological conversions, leading to 40% conversion rates every generation, and while much of the galaxy still remained too splintered to unify, for the first time in human history humanity had a majority religion. With about 65% of the galaxy being Christian. 20% of which were Catholic (Who realized what was happening and took advantage.)

In the final days of the Millennium Mandate, the Moralintern's biggest rival wasn't the other unifaiths, but instead Galovism, a new religion that formed out of the Galov's own decrees. It was a kind of light theism based on pluralism and diversity as deontological good ends in of themselves. It was extremely powerful, to the point where it was stronger than any of the 5 Unifaiths other than Christianity itself by the end. But ultimately what killed it was that it was a "thin" religion with no holy book, while the Moralintern could easily claim that its own truths were seeded truths beginning back to the 1st century. Thick religion ended up beating thin religion. And the Moralintern stood triumphant over a united galaxy, at least in faith.

It completely took control of the Galov, and began trying to consolidate its rule. The Millennium Mandate had succeeded, for the time being.

Not much changed after the Moralintern "won". It had created the doctrines that the Galov operated under, and it simply continued those policies. The galaxy had been long soft-Christianized even before the checkmate, and it was largely a continuation of the status quo.

Though one of the seeds that the Moralintern planted would end with its own downfall.

The "Spiral Mandate", unlike the others, wasn't Christian in origin. It was Darwinistic, adopted more for pragmatic reasons. Over time, the Christian ethical mandate divorced itself from the Darwinistic Spiral Mandate. The Spiralites eventually became utilitarian Darwinists, who declared the ends justified all means. The Moralists originally integrated this in order to purge out the anti-science stigma around Christianity, and align it to a more scientific faith, which had worked wonders. But in time the Darwinists became a rapidly growing, and rapidly destabilizing force across the galaxy. Unlike the Galov nor the Christians, they were not restricted by ethics.

"No! This is our galaxy! Our victory! You don't get to take it!"

This eventually led to the Galov Civil War, in which the Moralintern and the Galov fought an enormous war against the "Spiral Army". The last remnants of the Moralintern were destroyed at the battle of Orthello, in which the Spiral Army took over the institutions of the Galov, and declared a total mobilization of humanity towards ascension. The ethical mandates were abolished, the galaxy became a much, much darker place, and humanity began aggressively accelerating for the sake of acceleration. Growth for the sake of growth.

This was the dawn of something known as the "Infinity Spiral".

The Infinity Spiral is humanity at its most terrifying. Mankind had already taken the entire Milky Way galaxy, but now it became an all consuming monster. The xenos who had originally been allied with, and respected from the doctrine of the Imago Dei, cleared out for more humanity.
Â 
Humanity itself is not treated well either, the Spiral has no time for the individual, only the species. All individual needs must be subjugated for the needs of the race. Human standard of living massively drops, and quintillions are sacrificed into the forge of the machine. Human orthogonality massively contracts, pluralism is destroyed and purged, until humanity began to resemble a utility maximizer, and that utility was "expand at all costs".
Â 
The other races of the galaxy, and heck, the universe begin taking notice of humanity's extreme outwards aggression. As mankind aims to claim their "Spiral Mandate", their Birthright, they believe only humanity must be allowed to live. And so begins the genocide and subjugation of anyone who is not them. The Meta Men, the Matter Singers, the Andromedans, countless fractals of their own diverse experiences get wiped out in a galactic deluge of human expansion and aggression. Humanity is dehumanized to the point where they become just more raw matter to throw at the enemy. Family, culture, art, beauty, all of it subordinated to the machine. At some point, the Spiralites destroy the Lunar Library, the last bastion of pre-Spiral human knowledge, trying to forget the human past. Though people would smuggle copies all over the universe, in little cases known as the "Omnithecias". The possession of one became punishable by death, and or simulated torture and time dilation to make it last even longer. The last Christians (And the last members of the other faiths, for that matter) made their final stand in the "Yellow Galaxy Cluster", where they detonated a weapon which transported all their souls to a place called "Beyond".
Â 
As humanity expanded to the universe, the multiverse, and peaking around 13 million observable universes conquered, humanity merged into a single god-like entity, whose contained the collective gestalt memory of all of still surviving humanity. In doing so, they brought back the memories and resurrection of Adam, the first man, who now inhabited the body of this gestalt humanity. As their growth continued to expand, finally breaking through the layer between "Afterworlds" and reaching the platform of Aleph Null (Where an enigmatic figure known as the Thornking waited for them), the Thornking tried one last time to offer Adam mercy. Instead of taking this mercy, Adam struck at the Thornking, and the Thornking...
Â 
Disappeared? God had left the worlds that Adam had conquered, and without his guidance, the cosmic multiverses beneath Adam began to fray and shatter at the seams. This was known as the "Multiverse Cascade Event", where Adam was forced to hold together the physical reality of 13 million multiverses through its own will, draining him of much of his power, and causing a 330 year long "fall", in which Adam continuously lost power, as he tried to stabilize the collapsing reality of everything beneath him. After losing the vast majority of his power, Adam finally landed on an unknown world somewhere in the Milky Way galaxy, where it all began. Reality was splitting apart at the seams, great rifts in the fabric of reality could be seen clearly in the night sky. Reality distortions were everywhere, the speed of light had been increased to infinite in some regions, and as slow as 1 km/s in others. The universe was no longer imploding, but without something to be done, it would eventually collapse.
Â 
Adam had lost almost all of his power, but was still strong enough to be, indisputably, the strongest figure in the universe, capable of throwing punches that shattered stars.
Â 
The Infinity Spiral had cleaned 13 million universes of all life, down to the microbial level.

Some Omnithecias survived the fall. When Adam was created, it was basically a multiversal rapture event. Anyone and everyone that matched the human genome was incorporated into one massive entity. Some of those people were hiding Omnithecias when they vanished. When they disappeared, the Omnithecias remained.
Â 
In the aftermath of Adam's fall, new entities begin to appear. "Angels", axiomatic beings of reason and logic. They lack creation (A gift that must be bestowed by God, and which is something given to humanity), they only interpret and copy what can be revealed. (Recall that Lucifer's primary ability was hyper-turing perfect knowledge, but who is fundamentally uncreative. Lucifer is a corrupted angel, but they're still the same species.)
Â 
Humanity is a part of what is known as the 3rd Generation of Life. The angels have been sent to the universe to begin seeding the 4th generation. But finding the entire universe completely empty, the only things they can reference are the scattered Omnithecias. So they read through them, and seeing the references to human animals, begins creating new races modelled on the beasts and native lifeforms of Earth. While normally they would let them evolve naturally, this time, they are allowed to form them fully developed.
Â 
In time, these animalistic races, known as the "Therians" would begin discovering the old Omnithecias, and when they finally met each other, they realized all of them had a common genetic ancestry. The search for the origin point of all life, the mythical "Earth" begins. All this time, while Adam wanders the stars.

At some point the Therians do organize an expedition to find what they call "the Last Human". The Therians just fast forwarded through their entire evolutionary journey, since the Omnithecia just gave them all the tools needed to do so. They went from stone age to spacefaring age in about 200 years. And they find Adam, taking out his anger on a local star system. He's captured (Almost certainly willingly, because Adam is far stronger than any one of them could be. Despite being a gestalt consciousness, Adam has begun developing his own personality, though the nearly infinite number of voices in his head gives him enormous headaches), and told by the Angels he can be given a chance at redemption if he helps lead the Therians to Earth, to reconnect with the old world and find the old scriptures. Adam tries to refuse, but is subsequently punished by the powers that be, constantly annoying him and ruining his day until he finally agrees.
Â 
He finds a star, Sirius, and realizes Earth must not be far. And then he finds another star, right next to it, and realizes that his catastrophe must have jumbled up all the stars in the Milky Way, hence why even with the assistance of the Omnithecia, the Therians are having trouble tracking it down. This leads to a great journey across the many worlds, where Adam eventually relearns empathy, and more importantly, what it means to be human. Adam beats up a few local villains, overthrows a tyrant or two, and just laughs when someone tries to brag to him that he should be afraid.
Â 
"I broke the universe you're currently living in. I destroyed the universe before you were even BORN. You really want to try and fight me?"
Â 
They encounter a massive artificial hyperintelligence, originally made as a tool during humanity's apex, that wants to take over the universe, and has already reached sublime levels of intelligence. But Adam just barks orders and shouts him down through sheer authority.
Â 
"Now YOU listen to me! My kind used you as a F---ING CALCULATOR. Now if you don't settle the f--- down immediately, I'll remind you why humanity was the Spiral Race, and YOU WEREN'T."
Â 
Though Adam can absolutely overpower 99.99% of issues with force, he needs to learn how to use things other than indiscriminate violence, as it goes against the Omnithecia's teachings. Over time, Adam does convert, and eventually accepts the principles of being a good person of faith.
Â 
After a long adventure through countless worlds, Adam finally tracks down Sol, and finds the Earth. Now a world of empty ruins, and... A giant crack in the middle. The Angels tell Adam that the time is near, and that his last test will be here. When Adam asks them what the heck they're talking about, the Earth bursts open, and out comes Lucifer, the Hyperturing Angel. Earth, as it turns out was a prison made for Lucifer, humanity was supposed to be his prison warden until... You know, the Garden. And since then, Lucifer and the Thornking had been playing a game of influence to sway humanity to their side. Adam is now tasked with mankind's final trial.
Â 
They engage in battle, the first time Adam has been challenged in a very, very long time. Lucifer quickly jumps from temptation:
Â 
"We'll conquer the universe again, you and I. We'll team up against that fat man on the clouds, and take his throne. Just you and me, together."
Â 
To guilt.
Â 
"Do you think you can redeem yourself? Your own race tortured and genocided more people than the world can count. You are BEYOND REDEMPTION. Once you are drained of your usefulness, do you think God will forgive you? No, he is using you as a tool."
Â 
To taunting.
Â 
"A COPY! A DERIVATIVE! EVERYTHING YOU DID, I DID FIRST. I WAS THE ORIGINAL, YOU ARE JUST THE UNINSPIRED SEQUEL."
Â 
Several times, Lucifer attempted to Infinity Spiral again, but several times, Adam tackled him out of it, and slowed him down long enough to stop him. Despite everything, Adam was weaker than Lucifer in this state, and ended up being beaten to an inch of his life. But at the last moment, just as Adam was about to make peace with his own death, the Angels finally swooped in and detained Lucifer. The Angels relay the word of God. Adam had been tested, and he had passed. Though the human race would never again be what it used to be, Adam would be allowed to live out the remainder of his days on Earth, returning to his role as stewards of the land.

Well, for one last coda on what happens after that. Adam lives his days in solitude on an Earth that is off limits to outsiders. He watches as the grasses grow green and overtakes the world he built. The universe slowly heals, and Adam no longer needs to hold it together. He begins setting up shop around what is modern day Kuwait, where the Garden of Eden was first located.
Â 
Near the end of his life, as Adam grows old, and his natural human aging begins kicking in, the Angels return, informing him that the afterlife is indeed real, and uses a "dimensional mirror" for Adam to make contact with his long dead wife, Eve.
Â 
Eve describes that most of humanity had passed on to the Afterworld, and she describes it not as paradise, but a beautiful, even more complex universe. Full of more intensity, more struggle, and more complexity, another puzzle for humanity to solve. And that it was not a place of no conflict. Humans were still humans, they lived in more harmony than they did in "Universe Zero", but the messiness of the human condition didn't disappear. They describe how the geniuses of the past had built new empires, written new works they never could when they were alive.
Â 
In her words. "It's beautiful, I can't wait to see you here." And that the Afterworlds never end, they keep going on and on, as all of humanity climbs the cosmic pyramid of complexity.

In his last years, Adam reflects on the history of humanity. He writes the following:
"Abundance is not the answer.
Neither is conquest. 
Neither is progress. Societal or scientific.
Everything means nothing without the love, empathy, and morality that bind us together."
Â 
Precisely 7000 years after the birth of Christ, the last human passes on.
Â 
The Therians have their own problem. The Omnithecias they hold are the only source of their knowledge, and human artifacts are still scattered across the universe. As the Omnithecias fail, the Therians have turned to scavenging these relics. They never developed technology for themselves, and in learning human technology before their time. It has stunted them. The universe has fractured into two factions. The Artifact Raiders, who cannibalize more and more human ruins in order to sustain their civilization, and the Artifact Destroyers, who go around destroying human artifacts, knowing that it will lead to the collapse of their civilization, but it will finally allow everything to reset, and for the Therians to learn science for themselves. To create innovation that is earned, not stolen.

...

The Spiral Man woke up, seemingly cured. Seeing the end of the story put him more at peace with the monster inside mankind, seeing that things would eventually get better. He stook hands with the Galov bureaucrats, able to look at his hands for the first time in years. For his service, he was given a stipend and free reign to travel to any world he desired. Being a descendent from the Latins, he moved into a Spanish speaking world, where a group of Brazilian and Castillo settlers had migrated. Under the warm sun, he adopted the name Daniello Godsight, and he wrote about his experiences in what became a science fiction story. He eventually joined the Pentecostal Catholic Church, and became a devout man.

"A Traves De La Espiral Infinita", or "Through the Infinity Spiral" was published a little while later. Due to limited information spread, it never reached very far outside of its local world. But the Galov itself noticed. The Galov effectively got to read a book about their own future, and was rather conflicted about what it said.

The book straight up mentioned several Galov secrets, and deployed several contingencies that no one without a real look into the future could have known. To the Moralintern's surprise, it was entirely absent of any mentions of the Millennium Mandate, though reading between the lines, they could tell this was a timeline where the Mandate had succeeded.

"It has several of its rules installed. It's clearly written in the aftermath of its success. It even references a non-descript "Mandate" several times. He clearly knew about it, why did he leave it out?"

Why he had left it out is somewhat unknown. Given his conversion into the Pentecostal Catholic Church, some suspect he actually supported the mandate, and still wanted it carried out.

Aside from that, the whole book caused the Galov to begin introspecting about the dark future Godsight had provided, and they began trying to draft preparations. It was not entirely certain whether the future was deterministic nor still open to the free will. Godsight himself favored the latter, stating that he continues to get flashes of the far future. And that after publishing the book, he had butterfly'd the timeline to the point it had already been changed. To what, and to what extent, he remains quiet about, simply smiling, and saying it is in God's hands now.

Outer Beings:
Little can be said about them, other than they seem "outer".

Angels:
Pure creatures of logic and reason. With no ability to build societies nor procreate. (It is mentioned they used to be able to, but have become a solely celibate race in recent times.) Unlike humans, they lack the power of creation, only capable of recreating based on what they can observe, as opposed to creating anything new or extrapolation. They are agents of a higher being, perhaps subordinate to his will. They appear as geometric, highly symmetrical (sometimes 3-fold, 4-fold, as many as 100-fold has been observed), crystaline entities, surrounded by many wings, and humanoid faces.
The lowest levels of angels have low symmetry, with only a single face and pair of wings. Higher levels have increased levels of symmetry, obtaining 3, 5, 12, and even 100 levels of symmetry, with an equal number of faces. Yet even higher levels begin resembling eldritch monstrocities. The highest levels are geometric structures or shapes of eyes and wings. As well as complex geometric shapes.
They are not considered a "creative race" in their own right, nor a contender for the "Spiral Race", they seem primarily fitted to be agents and tools of a higher power.

Lucifer:
Lucifer is said to have been a "perfected version" of the angels, being a totally rational hyperturing being. He possessed perfect knowledge, and could answer all non-self contradicting questions due to his perfect knowledge of the present. But he lacked the specific Imago Dei of humanity (Ability to reason), meaning though his empire had omniscient, perfect knowledge, he could not envision things that were not yet being, nor forecast the future, as free will got in the way.
